   A.   Accumulation Prohibited: Permit or suffer to accumulate in or about any
yard, lot, place or premises or upon any street, alley or sidewalk adjacent to
such lot, yard, place or premises, owned or occupied by such person, any
garbage or refuse so as to cause such yard, lot, place or premises to cause or
create a nuisance or offensive odor, atmosphere or rodent harborage or thereby
be or become or cause or create a public nuisance. (1983 Code § 8.04.100)
   B.   Throwing Or Depositing: Throw away, dump or discard any type or nature
of garbage or refuse on any public lands, rights of way or private land
belonging to another. (1983 Code § 8.04.110)
3-1-7: VIOLATION; PENALTY:
It is unlawful and shall constitute a misdemeanor for any person to violate the
provisions of this chapter. Upon conviction of violations of this chapter, the
offender shall be punished as provided in the general penalty in section
1-3-1 of this code. In addition thereto, the court shall have power to issue an
injunction against further or continued violation of the terms or intent of
this chapter. (1983 Code § 8.04.110)
CHAPTER 2
NUISANCES
SECTION:
3-2-1: Animal Refuse
3-2-2: Offensive Or Dangerous Accumulations
3-2-3: Obstructions
3-2-4: Open Burning
3-2-5: Trees
3-2-6: Noxious Weeds
3-2-7: Violation; Penalty
3-2-1: ANIMAL REFUSE:
No person shall cast or leave or keep in or adjoining any street, lane, square
or public place, or in any yard, lot, block or other premises within the city
limits any putrid, unsound, unwholesome or refuse meat of any animal, or any
hides or skins of any kind, or the whole or any part of any dead fish or
animal, or any stagnant or impure water, or garbage or the offensive waste or
manure of any animal or animals. (1983 Code § 8.12.010)
3-2-2: OFFENSIVE OR DANGEROUS ACCUMULATIONS:
   A.   Garbage And Stagnant Water: No person shall permit or suffer to
accumulate in or upon any yard or premises, lot or places within the city
limits or upon any street or sidewalk adjacent to or abutting upon any lot,
block, place or premises occupied by him, or for which he may be agent or
agents, within the city limits, any stagnant or impure water, refuse,
vegetables, decayed or decaying substances, garbage or filth of any kind; shall
not suffer such yard, lot or premises to be or to remain in such condition as
to cause or create a noisome or offensive smell or atmosphere, or thereby to be
or become, cause or create a public nuisance. (1983 Code § 8.12.020)
   B.   Explosive Substances: It is unlawful for any person to keep or store in
any building, or elsewhere, within the city limits, more than twenty five (25)
pounds of gunpowder, nitroglycerin, dynamite, blasting powder or other highly
explosive substance, and when so kept or stored, it must be placed in some iron
receptacle, so that in case of fire it can be conveniently moved. (1983 Code §
8.12.040)
   C.   Inflammable Materials: It is unlawful to allow an accumulation of
brush, fallen limbs, slashings and other inflammable material within the city
limits. (1983 Code § 8.12.050)
3-2-3: OBSTRUCTIONS:
   A.   Streets: It is unlawful for any person to obstruct any of the streets
and avenues in the city limits by placing and leaving thereon any lumber, logs,
poles, wagons, machinery and such other articles and matter which will have a
tendency to obstruct or blockade such streets and avenues. (1983 Code §
8.12.030; amd. 2004 Code)
   B.   Gutters And Drains: It is prohibited and unlawful for any person to
obstruct any of the gutters on any street within the city or in any artificial
watercourse, or carrier or conductor of surface water, or any pipe, drain or
other carrier or conductor of water on, above or underneath any street or
property within the city by placing therein or thereon any dirt, refuse, snow,
ice or any matter or thing which shall in any manner prevent the free discharge
and drainage of water through, over, upon or in such gutters, pipes or other
watercourses or drains. (1983 Code § 8.12.060)
3-2-4: OPEN BURNING:
Burning of paper, grass, brush, lumber or other burnable refuse shall be
prohibited between June 1 and September 30 unless a burning permit is issued by
the city clerk. The burning of paper, grass, brush, lumber or other burnable
refuse shall be permitted without a permit between October 1 and May 31. (1983
Code § 8.12.100)
3-2-5: TREES:
   A.   Nuisances Declared: All trees growing in a natural state on lots
adjoining residences or buildings on other lots, all or any part of which is
likely to fall and injure such buildings or to fall on the property of others,
or to do injury to life or property of others, are hereby declared to be a
public nuisance. (1983 Code § 8.12.070)
   B.   Removal Required: The mayor is hereby authorized, empowered and
directed, on request of any resident of the city owning property menaced by
such standing trees to serve on such party or parties owning or occupying such
land on which said trees are located, a notice requiring their immediate
destruction; provided that, should said owner or occupier be a nonresident or
not found in the city, notice may be served by mailing same to his last known
address. The notice shall require the removal of said trees within five (5)
days from receipt of notice. In default of removing said trees after notice,
the mayor may proceed forthwith to hire such labor as may be required, to
remove the same and abate the nuisance, all at the property owner's expense.
(1983 Code § 8.12.080)
   C.   Removal Of Certain Trees By Private Citizens: The owner of any lot or
building near or adjacent or contiguous to said trees and likely to be damaged
by the falling of said trees, may secure permission of the mayor or city
council to, and at his own expense may, remove and abate said nuisance and cut
such trees. (1983 Code § 8.12.090)
3-2-6: NOXIOUS WEEDS:
   A.   Noxious Growths Defined: The following named weeds and growths shall be
considered noxious within the meaning of this section: wild mustard, thistles,
and all growths commonly known as weeds. (1983 Code § 8.08.010)
   B.   Failure To Cut: Any person who shall, within the city limits, allow any
noxious growths to grow and remain uncut on any property owned in whole or in
part, or occupied by such person, shall be deemed guilty of maintaining a
nuisance; and the continuance of the same for every day after having been
notified by the mayor to cut or destroy such noxious growths, shall be
considered as a separate offense. (1983 Code § 8.08.020)
   C.   Noxious Growths On Public Ways: It shall be the duty of the mayor to
cut or destroy all noxious growths upon the streets, alleys and public highways
of the city, and for such purposes he may employ and hire all labor and help as
may be necessary under the direction of the city council. (1983 Code §
8.08.030)
   D.   Notice Of Violation: Before a person is convicted of an offense as
defined in subsection B of this section, it shall be made to appear that such
person shall have been served with a reasonable notice, either verbal or
written, from the mayor to abate the same; and that he failed or neglected to
do so; and in case of violation of subsection B of this section, the mayor
shall enter a complaint before a proper magistrate to enforce the penalty set
out herein. (1983 Code § 8.08.040; amd. 2004 Code)
3-2-7: VIOLATION; PENALTY:
Except as otherwise provided in this chapter, any person violating any of the
provisions of this chapter shall be deemed guilty of a misdemeanor and, upon
conviction thereof, shall be punished as provided in the general penalty in
section
1-3-1 of this code. (1983 Code § 8.12.110)
CHAPTER 3
NOISE CONTROL
SECTION:
3-3-1: Title
3-3-2: Definitions
3-3-3: Antinoise Regulations
3-3-4: Exceptions
3-3-5: Penalties
3-3-1: TITLE:
This chapter shall be known and cited as the HARRISON ANTINOISE AND PUBLIC
NUISANCE ORDINANCE. (Ord. 2019-476, 5-7-2019)
3-3-2: DEFINITIONS:
The following terms used in this chapter are defined as follows:
NOISE SENSITIVE UNIT: Any building or portion thereof, vehicle, boat or other
structure used as a business, church, daycare center, hospital, farm property
with animals, nursing care center, school, or place used for overnight
accommodations of persons, including, but not limited to, individual homes,
individual apartments, trailers and nursing homes.
PLAINLY AUDIBLE: Any sound for which the information content of that sound is
unambiguously communicated to the listener, such as, but not limited to,
understandable spoken speech, comprehensible musical rhythms or vocal sounds.
(Ord. 2019-476, 5-7-2019)
3-3-3: ANTINOISE REGULATIONS:
   A.   General Regulation: It is unlawful for any person to make, continue or
cause to be made or continued, any noise, which unreasonably annoys, disturbs,
injures or endangers the comfort, repose, health, peace or safety of any person
of normal sensitivity in a noise sensitive unit. The standard which shall be
utilized in determining whether a violation of the provisions of this chapter
exists shall include, but not be limited to, the following:
      1.   The volume of the noise;
      2.   The intensity of the noise;
      3.   Whether the origin of the noise is usual or unusual;
      4.   Whether the origin of the noise is natural or unnatural;
      5.   The volume and intensity of the background noise, if any;
      6.   Whether the noise is plainly audible within a noise sensitive unit;
      7.   The nature and zoning of the area within which the noise emanates;
      8.   The density of the inhabited area within which the noise emanates;
      9.   The time of day or night the noise occurs;
      10.   The duration of the noise;
      11.   Whether the noise is recurrent, intermittent, or constant.
   B.   Specific Violations: The following noises and disturbances are hereby
declared to be a violation of this chapter; provided, however, that the
specification of the same is not hereby to be construed to exclude other
violations of this chapter not specifically enumerated:
      1.   Electronic Or Mechanical Devices: The playing of any radio,
phonograph, television or other electronic or mechanical sound producing
device, including any sound amplifying device upon any vehicle on the streets
of the City, or any musical instrument, in such a manner or with such volume as
to unreasonably disturb the quiet, comfort or repose of other persons.
      2.   Yelling On Public Street: Yelling, shouting, hooting or singing on
the public street between the hours of ten o'clock (10:00) P.M. and seven
o'clock (7:00) A.M. or at any time or place so as to unreasonably upset or
disturb the quiet, comfort or repose of any persons in the vicinity.
      3.   Animals: The keeping of any animal, bird or fowl which emanates
frequent or extended noise which shall disturb the quiet, comfort or repose of
any person in the vicinity, such as allowing or permitting any dog to bark
repeatedly in any area where such barking can be clearly heard from nearby
residential property.
      4.   Construction: The erection, excavation, demolition, alteration or
repair of any building or premises in any part of the City, including the
streets and highways, in such a manner as to emanate noise or disturbance to
other persons, between the hours of ten o'clock (10:00) P.M. and seven o'clock
(7:00) A.M. on any day, except in cases of urgent necessity in the interest of
public health and safety. In such case, a permit shall be obtained from the
City Clerk or Code Enforcement Officer in the City, which permit shall limit
the periods that the activity may continue.
      5.   Machinery: The operation of any machinery, equipment or mechanical
device so as to emit unreasonably loud noise which is disturbing to the comfort
or repose of any person between the hours of ten o'clock (10:00) P.M. and seven
o'clock (7:00) A.M.
      6.   Other: Making any noise between the hours of ten o'clock (10:00)
P.M. and seven o'clock (7:00) A.M., such that the noise level is plainly
audible more than one hundred feet (100') from the sound origination point.
(Ord. 2019-476, 5-7-2019)
3-3-4: EXCEPTIONS:
   A.   Nothing in this chapter shall prohibit the City from allowing amplified
sound systems to be operated on public or private property in association with
a special event, schedule of events, or other permitted event or activity,
subject to such reasonable conditions as the City may deem necessary and
appropriate.
   B.   This chapter shall not apply to emergency vehicles or City vehicles
being operated in their work and/or designated capacity. (Ord. 2019-476, 5-7-
2019)
3-3-5: PENALTIES:
Any person found violating the provisions of this chapter shall, upon
conviction, be deemed guilty of an infraction and issued a fine of one hundred
dollars ($100.00). Each day that a violation shall continue is to constitute a
separate offense. Provisions of this chapter may also be enforced by suit for
injunction, damages or other appropriate legal action. (Ord. 2019-476, 5-7-
2019)
CHAPTER 4
FIREWORKS
SECTION:
3-4-1: Title And Authority
3-4-2: Purpose And Jurisdiction
3-4-3: Definitions
3-4-4: Retail Sales
3-4-5: Public Displays And Other Events
3-4-6: Conditions Of Permits
3-4-7: Prohibited Acts And Conditions
3-4-8: Penalties
3-4-1: TITLE AND AUTHORITY:
This chapter shall be known as the FIREWORKS ORDINANCE of the city of Harrison,
and is authorized under Idaho Code title 50, chapter 3. (Ord. 393, 3-2-2004)
3-4-2: PURPOSE AND JURISDICTION:
The purpose of this chapter is to protect the general health, safety and public
welfare of residents of the city and visitors by regulating the use, possession
and sale of fireworks, and this chapter shall apply to the storage, use,
possession and sale of fireworks within any incorporated areas within the city.
(Ord. 393, 3-2-2004)
3-4-3: DEFINITIONS:
The following definitions shall apply within this chapter:
CITY: The city of Harrison, Idaho.
DEPARTMENT: The department of insurance, division of the state fire marshal.
FIREWORKS: Any combustible or explosive composition, or any substance or
combination of substances or article prepared for the purpose of producing a
visible or audible effect by combustion, explosion, deflagration or detonation.
Fireworks includes items classified as common or special fireworks by the
United States bureau of explosives or contained in the regulation of the United
States department of transportation and designated as UN 0335 1.3G or UN 0336
1.4G. The term "fireworks" shall not include any automotive safety flares, toy
guns, toy cannons, caps or other items designed for use with toy guns or toy
cannons, party poppers, popits or other devices which contain twenty-five
hundredths (0.25) of a grain or less explosive substance.
NONAERIAL COMMON FIREWORKS: Any fireworks such as ground spinners, fountains,
sparklers, smoke devices or snakes designed to remain on or near the ground and
not to travel outside a fifteen foot (15') diameter circle above a height of
twenty feet (20').
PERMIT: An authorization given by the authority having jurisdiction pursuant to
Idaho Code 39-2604 or 39-2605.
SPECIAL FIREWORKS: Any firework designed primarily for display and classified
as special fireworks by the United States bureau of explosives or designated as
UN 0335 1.3G. (Ord. 393, 3-2-2004)
3-4-4: RETAIL SALES:
   A.   Permit Required: The city hereby requires a permit for the retail sale
of nonaerial common fireworks.
   B.   Application: An application for a permit hereunder shall include the
name and address of the applicant; or the names of all partners, if a
partnership; the name of the corporation and the corporate officers, if a
corporation; or the name of the limited liability company and all of its
members, if a limited liability company; the primary location of the business;
each location at which fireworks are to be stored; and the applicant's Idaho
sales tax seller's permit number, if applicable.
   C.   Insurance: A bond or valid certificate of public liability and property
casualty insurance providing coverage of up to five hundred thousand dollars
($500,000.00) for personal injury and property damage shall be required at the
time of application:
   D.   Fee: The city shall assess a fee for issuing a permit under this
section which shall not exceed fifty dollars ($50.00). This fee may be amended
from time to time by resolution of the city council.
   E.   Valid Dates: The permit shall be issued if the application is complete
in compliance with applicable law, shall be valid for twelve (12) months from
the date of issuance and shall be nontransferable.
   F.   Display: The permit shall be displayed in public view at the location
listed on the permit.
   G.   Revocation: The permit required under this section may be revoked if
the permittee violates any provisions of this chapter or of state or federal
law. (Ord. 393, 3-2-2004)
3-4-5: PUBLIC DISPLAYS OR OTHER EVENTS:
The city may, at its discretion, issue a permit for a public display or other
event in the following circumstances:
   A.   After determining that the public display will be supervised by a
qualified person and will not constitute an unreasonable hazard to persons or
property. Appropriate national fire protection association or uniform fire code
provisions may be used as guidance for this determination.
   B.   After determining that sales and use of fireworks outside the normal
sales period provided in Idaho Code 39-2606, or proposing the use of fireworks
in addition to nonaerial common fireworks will not constitute an unreasonable
hazard to persons or property.
   C.   An application for a permit for public display or other event shall be
on a form approved by and contain the information reasonably requested by the
city.
   D.   The permit shall be nontransferable, shall list the specific date or
dates upon which the display or event shall occur and the types of fireworks
and uses that will be allowed.
   E.   A bond or valid certificate of public liability and property casualty
insurance providing coverage of up to one million dollars ($1,000,000.00) for
personal injury and property damage may be required at the time of application
for public display of special fireworks.
   F.   The city may assess a fee for issuing a permit for public display under
this section which shall not exceed one hundred fifty dollars ($150.00).
   G.   Alteration of fireworks may be performed by a person in possession of a
valid public display permit.
   H.   If a public display or other event using fireworks is to be held over a
lake, river or other navigable waterway in the city, the applicant must obtain
a marine event permit from the Kootenai County sheriff. (Ord. 393, 3-2-2004)
3-4-6: CONDITIONS OF PERMITS:
   A.   Authorized Dates: Nonaerial common fireworks may be sold at retail and
used beginning at twelve o'clock (12:00) midnight on June 23 and ending at
twelve o'clock (12:00) midnight on July 5, and beginning at twelve o'clock (12:
00) midnight on December 26 and ending at twelve o'clock (12:00) midnight on
January 1.
   B.   Temporary Fireworks Stands: Temporary fireworks stands shall be
governed by Idaho Code 39-2607.
   C.   Short Term Storage: Short term storage of fireworks shall be governed
by Idaho Code 39-2608. (Ord. 393, 3-2-2004)
3-4-7: PROHIBITED ACTS AND CONDITIONS:
Except in compliance with this chapter, it shall be unlawful for any person to:
   A.   Alter any fireworks;
   B.   Throw any fireworks from, into or at a moving vehicle or at any person;
   C.   Sell, use or possess any fireworks at a time not permitted under this
chapter;
   D.   Use fireworks in any area that constitutes a severe fire threat based
on the vegetative conditions during the current fire season, as determined by
the county commission or authority having jurisdiction, provided that notice of
such areas is given in advance or the area is posted with appropriate notices
at points of access.
   E.   Fail to obtain a permit from the authority having jurisdiction for a
public display or other event using fireworks before holding the public display
or other event using fireworks.
   F.   Fail to obtain a permit from the authority having jurisdiction before
engaging in retail sales of nonaerial common fireworks. (Ord. 393, 3-2-2004)
3-4-8: PENALTIES:
Any person violating the provisions of this chapter or the rules issued
hereunder shall be guilty of a misdemeanor punishable as provided in the
general penalty in section
1-3-1 of this code. Fireworks being used, sold or possessed in violation of
this chapter may be confiscated by the city or by any peace officer. (Ord. 393,
3-2-2004)
TITLE 4
POLICE REGULATIONS
CHAPTER 1A
ANIMAL CONTROL
ARTICLE A. DOGS
SECTION:
4-1A-1: License Requirements
4-1A-2: Dogs At Large
4-1A-3: Dogs On Public Or Private Property
4-1A-4: Impoundment Procedures
4-1A-5: Enforcement; Penalty
4-1A-1: LICENSE REQUIREMENTS:
   A.   Required; Term And Fees: It is unlawful for any person to own, harbor
or keep in his possession or under his control any dog of either sex without
having first paid an annual license fee provided in subsection B of this
section therefor to the city, which said license fee shall authorize the
keeping of said dog, but only one dog per person maximum, for only one year
from the date thereof, and all licenses issued under and by virtue of this
article shall date from the first Monday in January of each year and expire on
December 31 of the same year. (Ord. 334, 3-7-1995)
   B.   License Fees: Every person owning, harboring, keeping or having in his
possession or under his control any dog, shall immediately upon becoming the
owner, harborer or keeper, pay to the city treasurer the license fee as
follows:
 
An unspayed female dog          $5.00
A male dog or spayed female dog 3.00
 
   On the first Monday in January of each year, the owner shall also provide,
at the time of licensing, proof that the dog's rabies shots are current. All
persons becoming the owner of or harboring a dog on or after the first Monday
in January of each year must take out a license for the animal within ten (10)
days after becoming the owner, harborer or keeper of the animal. (Ord. 352, 2-
3-1998)
   C.   Contents; Issuance: It shall be the duty of the city clerk, upon the
payment of said license fee, to issue to the person paying the same a receipt,
which receipt shall specify the date thereof, the amount paid, a description of
the dog for which said license is issued sufficient for identification, the
name of said dog, together with the name of the person obtaining said license,
and the sex of the dog. At the time of issuing the receipt, the city clerk
shall furnish and deliver to such party a license in the shape of a metal tag,
bearing the words "Harrison Dog Tax," and the year for which the same is issued
stamped thereon. (1983 Code § 6.04.030)
   D.   Tag Required To Be Worn: The person to whom said license is issued
shall cause said tag to be attached to a collar to be worn by the dog for which
said license fee was paid, during the time which said dog is allowed to run;
and it is unlawful for any dog of either sex to run at large within the city
limits unless the metal tag so issued is attached to its collar. (1983 Code §
6.04.040)
   E.   Records Kept: It shall be the duty of the city clerk to keep a register
of each license issued, which shall contain a description of the dog covered by
said license, sufficient for identification, and shall state the sex of the
dog, its name and the name of the person obtaining said license, together with
the date and expiration of the license. (1983 Code § 6.04.050)
   F.   Compliance Required: Any person owning, harboring, keeping or having in
his possession or under his control any dog of either sex without having paid
upon said dog the license fee for the current year as provided in the
subsection B of this section, or without having said metal tag for the current
year attached to the collar worn by said dog, and without having complied with
all the other provisions of this chapter, shall be guilty of a misdemeanor and,
in addition to the penalty prescribed, shall be compelled to pay the license on
said dog for the current year. (1983 Code § 6.04.060)
4-1A-2: DOGS AT LARGE:
   A.   Prohibited: Any person who wilfully or negligently permits any dog
owned, possessed or harbored by him to be or run at large within the limits of
the city, or who wilfully and negligently fails and refuses to keep such dog
securely confined within the limits of his own premises, shall be guilty of a
misdemeanor. (1983 Code § 6.04.070)
   B.   Destruction Of Dog; Exception: It shall be the duty of the mayor to
kill, or cause to be killed, all dogs of either sex found running at large
which cannot, by reasonable means, be impounded and dealt with pursuant to
section 4-1A-4 of this article; but nothing herein contained shall authorize
the killing of any dog owned or kept by any person residing outside of the city
when such person shall have brought such dog into the city the intention of
moving him therefrom forthwith. (1983 Code § 6.04.080)
   C.   Vicious Dogs Prohibited: Any person being the owner or keeper of any
vicious dog who shall permit the same to run at large within the limits of the
city shall be guilty of a misdemeanor. (1983 Code § 6.04.090)
   D.   Dogs In Heat: It shall be unlawful for any owner or keeper of any
female dog to knowingly permit it to run at large while in heat,
notwithstanding such person may have a license for such dog as provided in this
article. (1983 Code § 6.04.100)
4-1A-3: DOGS ON PUBLIC OR PRIVATE PROPERTY:
It is unlawful for any owner to allow or permit any dog, whether licensed or
not, to be or remain upon any street or alley within the city or upon any
public place thereon, or upon any premises other than the premises of the owner
of such dog or the one having charge thereof unless:
   A.   Such dog is in the charge of a person and controlled by a leash not
exceeding eight feet (8') in length; or
   B.   Such dog is confined in a motor vehicle. (1983 Code § 6.04.110)
4-1A-4: IMPOUNDMENT PROCEDURES:
   A.   It shall be the duty of the mayor, or any suitable person under his
direction, to impound any dog running at large in violation of the provisions
of this article, and to hold such dog for a period of two (2) days, and
immediately notify the owner of such dog, if the owner's name is disclosed in
the registry of licensed dogs, that such dog is held and impounded. If the dog
is held for the reason that it is running loose unleashed, in violation of the
provisions of this chapter, the owner thereof may, within said period of time,
redeem said dog by paying the impounding officer the charges of impounding said
animal.
   B.   If, within the said time, the dog is not redeemed by the owner as above
provided, the mayor or any suitable person under his direction, shall cause
said dog to be killed in a humane manner and its carcass buried or otherwise
disposed of. (1983 Code § 6.04.120)
4-1A-5: ENFORCEMENT; PENALTY:
   A.   Administration: The city council shall have power to appoint and employ
competent persons to enforce the provisions of this article. (1983 Code §
6.04.130)
   B.   Violation; Penalty: Any person violating any of the provisions of this
article shall be deemed guilty of a misdemeanor and, upon conviction thereof,
shall be punished as provided in the general penalty in section
1-3-1 of this code. Every day upon which any person violates any of the
provisions of this article shall constitute a separate offense. (1983 Code §
6.04.140)
CHAPTER 1B
ANIMAL CONTROL
ARTICLE B. DOMESTICATED AND FERAL CATS
SECTION:
4-1B-1: Definitions
4-1B-2: Responsibilities Of Domesticated Cat Owners
4-1B-3: Harboring Of Feral Cats Prohibited
4-1B-4: Enforcement; Penalty
4-1B-1: DEFINITIONS:
ATTRACTANT: Any substance, including, but not limited to, food, garbage,
blankets, heating devices or shelter which draws feral cats to a particular
location whether intended or not.
DOMESTICATED CAT: A cat that is socialized to humans, is generally under the
physical control and restraint of the owner, and is regularly provided food by
its owner.
FERAL CAT: A cat that is born in or has reverted to the wild, and is not
domesticated or tamed.
NUISANCE: Conduct by stray or feral cats that disturb the public health, safety
or welfare including, but not limited to, habitually or continually howling or
crying or habitually and significantly destroying, desecrating or soiling
property against the wishes of the owner of the property.
OWNER: Any person having a right of property in an animal or who keeps or
harbors an animal or who has it in his care, or acts as its custodian, or who
knowingly permits an animal to remain on any premises owned or controlled by
him.
STRAY CAT: A cat that is regularly off the property of the owner, is not under
the physical control and restraint of the owner, and is not regularly provided
food by its owner. (Ord. 448, 9-17-2012)
4-1B-2: RESPONSIBILITIES OF DOMESTICATED CAT OWNERS:
   A.   An owner of a domesticated cat shall provide appropriate and adequate
food, water and shelter to the cat.
   B.   An owner of a domesticated cat shall exercise reasonable care to guard
against the cat creating a nuisance.
   C.   An owner of a domesticated cat shall not abandon the cat. (Ord. 448, 9-
17-2012)
4-1B-3: HARBORING OF FERAL CATS PROHIBITED:
   A.   It shall be unlawful to feed or provide food, water or other
attractants to feral or stray cats within the city limits.
   B.   It is unlawful to wilfully or inadvertently provide shelter or other
protection for feral or stray cats.
   C.   Property owner and tenants of property are required to mitigate access
to their property by feral or stray cats. (Ord. 448, 9-17-2012)
4-1B-4: ENFORCEMENT; PENALTY:
   A.   Administration: The city council shall have the power to appoint and
employ competent persons to enforce the provisions of this article.
   B.   Impound: The city council and/or its designee has the authority to trap
and remove any cat where:
      1.   The cat has not been vaccinated against rabies or which is
demonstrating signs of the disease;
      2.   The cat is not spayed or neutered;
      3.   The cat is creating a nuisance; or
      4.   Removal is necessary for public health or public safety reasons.
   C.   Violation; Penalty: Any person violating any of the provisions of this
article shall be deemed guilty of a misdemeanor and, upon conviction thereof,
shall be punished as provided in the general penalty in section
1-3-1 of this code. Every day upon which a person violates any of the
provisions of this article shall constitute a separate offense. (Ord. 448, 9-
17-2012)
CHAPTER 1C
ANIMAL CONTROL
ARTICLE C. OTHER ANIMALS
SECTION:
4-1C-1: Cruelty To Animals
4-1C-2: Horses And Cows
4-1C-3: Livestock
4-1C-1: CRUELTY TO ANIMALS:
Any person who shall cruelly beat, torture, misuse, deprive of food and water
or otherwise treat any animal with cruelty within the city limits shall be
deemed guilty of a misdemeanor and shall be punished as provided in the general
penalty in section
1-3-1 of this code. (1983 Code § 6.16.010; amd. Ord. 448, 9-17-2012)
4-1C-2: HORSES AND COWS:
   A.   Barn Requirements; Location Restrictions: Any person keeping within the
city limits one or more horses or cows shall have and maintain a barn or place
where said animals shall be kept; and said barn or building where such animals
are so kept shall be at least fifty feet (50') from any building occupied as a
residence in the city, or any lot belonging to another person and suitable as a
residential building site. (1983 Code § 6.08.010; amd. Ord. 448, 9-17-2012)
   B.   Violations; Penalty: Any person violating any provisions of this
section shall be guilty of a misdemeanor, and upon conviction thereof shall be
punished as provided in the general penalty in section
1-3-1 of this code. (1983 Code § 6.08.040; amd. Ord. 448, 9-17-2012)
4-1C-3: LIVESTOCK:
   A.   Running At Large: No horses, cattle, sheep, hogs, poultry or animals or
fowl of a similar nature shall be allowed to run at large in any of the
streets, lanes or alleys of the city. No person shall permit the animals or
fowl described to run at large, and all animals so running at large may be
taken up by the mayor and impounded with proper care, food and water while so
confined. (1983 Code § 6.12.010; amd. Ord. 448, 9-17-2012)
   B.   Impoundment:
      1.   Owner Notified: The mayor shall immediately give notice to the
owners of any impounded animals, if known, and if such owners are not known, by
posting notice in three (3) conspicuous places in the city. (1983 Code §
6.12.020; amd. Ord. 448, 9-17-2012)
      2.   Disposition: At the expiration of five (5) days, after giving
official notice, the mayor shall sell, for cash at public auction to the
highest bidder, the animals so impounded. The mayor shall collect the same fees
for the making and posting of the notices mentioned in subsection B1 of this
section as are allowed by law to constables for sale notices and legal fees for
any notice published in a newspaper and for all costs incurred impounding said
animals. Out of the proceeds of any sale of such animal or animals or poultry
under this section, the mayor shall deduct all the costs and charges aforesaid;
and shall, if the owner is unknown to him, pay the remainder into the city
treasury, and, in case the owner is known, to such owner. (1983 Code §
6.12.030; amd. Ord. 448, 9-17-2012)
      3.   Redemption: The owner of such animals or fowl may redeem such
animals or fowl at any time before the sale by satisfactory proof of his
ownership and payment of the cost of care and keeping of such animals and fowl,
the costs incurred in posting and publishing notices and the sum of ten dollars
($10.00). (1983 Code § 6.12.040; amd. Ord. 448, 9-17-2012)
   C.   Keeping Of Pigs And Hogs: It is unlawful for any person to keep any
pigs or hogs within the city limits. (1983 Code § 6.12.050; amd. Ord. 448, 9-
17-2012)
   D.   Prohibited Acts: It is unlawful for any person to do any of the
following acts:
      1.   Herd cattle or horses within the city limits;
      2.   Stake out upon any public thoroughfare of the city any cow, horse,
cattle, horses or stock of any kind;
      3.   Stake out on any vacant lot or lots within the city limits any cows,
horses or any other kind of stock in such a manner as to permit said animals to
go upon, or to cross, any of the walks or public thoroughfares of the city;
      4.   Tie up or hitch any horse or mule upon any of the public streets of
the city; (1983 Code § 6.12.060; amd. Ord. 448, 9-17-2012)
      5.   Leave any horse team or teams hitched to any vehicle of any kind
unattended upon any of the public streets of the city. (1983 Code § 6.12.060;
amd. 2004 Code; Ord. 448, 9-17-2012)
   E.   Violation; Penalty: In addition to the provisions provided for in
subsection B of this section, a wilful violation of any of the other provisions
of this section, upon conviction, shall be punished as provided in the general
penalty in section
1-3-1 of this code. (1983 Code § 6.12.070; amd. Ord. 448, 9-17-2012)
CHAPTER 2
GENERAL OFFENSES
SECTION:
4-2-1: Littering
4-2-2: Public Consumption Of Alcoholic Beverages (Rep. by Ord. 406, 10-4-2005)
4-2-3: Curfew For Minors
4-2-1: LITTERING:
Any person who shall throw or deposit in any street, alley, sidewalk or
pedestrianway of the city any broken glass, bottles, crockery, nails or other
substance whatever whereby automobile tires or the feet of horses, pedestrians
or any beast of burden may be injured; or shall throw, deposit or sweep into or
upon any street, sidewalk or footpath of the city any paper or other substance
whatever, except snow or dirt, shall be deemed guilty of a misdemeanor; and
upon conviction thereof shall be punished as provided in the general penalty in
section
1-3-1 of this code. (1983 Code § 9.16.010)
4-2-2: PUBLIC CONSUMPTION OF ALCOHOLIC BEVERAGES:
(Rep. by Ord. 406, 10-4-2005)
4-2-3: CURFEW FOR MINORS:
   A.   Curfew Designated: It is unlawful for any person under the age of
sixteen (16) years or compulsory school age to be upon, loiter or stroll upon
the streets, alleys, avenues, parks or other public places in the city, after
the hour of ten o'clock (10:00) P.M. and before the hour of five o'clock (5:00)
A.M., unless such person shall be accompanied by a parent, legal guardian or
other adult person lawfully and properly accompanying said minor person;
provided, that the curfew shall be extended to eleven o'clock (11:00) P.M. and
before the hour of five o'clock (5:00) A.M. on any night designated by school
officials as an "activity night", by notification to the police authorities by
the school officials. (1983 Code § 9.36.010; amd. 2004 Code)
   B.   Parental Responsibility: It is unlawful for any parent, legal guardian
or any other adult person having the legal care and custody of any minor person
under the age of sixteen (16) years, to allow or permit any such person to go
upon, or be upon any street, alley, park or in any public place in the city
after the hour of ten o'clock (10:00) P.M. and before the hour of five o'clock
(5:00) A.M., without being accompanied by the parent, legal guardian or other
adult person. (1983 Code § 9.36.020; amd. 2004 Code)
   C.   Violators Taken Into Custody; Parents Notified: Any police officer or
other law enforcement officer is authorized and empowered to take charge of any
person under the age of sixteen (16) years violating the provisions of this
section, and it shall be the duty of such officers to take such person to the
police or city hall, and notify immediately the parent, guardian or adult
person having the care and custody of such minor of the violation of the terms
of this section and to inform the said person that the minor will be held at
the police or city hall until called for by such parent, guardian or legal
custodian. (1983 Code § 9.36.030)
   D.   Failure To Take Charge Of Minor: It is unlawful and shall be considered
a separate offense under this section for any parent, guardian, or other adult
person having the legal care and custody of any person under the age of sixteen
(16) years to refuse to come immediately, upon being notified to do so by the
police, to the police or city hall and take charge of such minor. (1983 Code §
9.36.040)
TITLE 5
MOTOR VEHICLES AND TRAFFIC
CHAPTER 1
GENERAL TRAFFIC REGULATIONS
SECTION:
5-1-1: State Vehicle Laws Adopted
5-1-2: Municipal Authority
5-1-3: Obedience To Traffic Officers
5-1-4: One-Way Streets
5-1-5: Speed Limits
5-1-6: Leaving Vehicles Unattended
5-1-7: Violation; Penalty
5-1-1: STATE VEHICLE LAWS ADOPTED:
   A.   Intent: It is hereby declared to be the intent of the city council to
aid and assist by whatever means possible for the utmost consistency in traffic
regulation among and between agencies of Idaho having such jurisdiction. Toward
that end, adoption of the Idaho motor vehicle laws by the cities of Idaho is a
necessary means of assuring maximum uniformity within the state.
   B.   Adoption Of Laws: There is hereby adopted for the purpose of
establishing rules and regulations for the use of all streets and public
thoroughfares of the city, that certain code, identified as the latest edition
of the Idaho motor vehicle laws, more particularly Idaho Code title 49,
published by the Idaho department of transportation, and as the same may
hereafter be revised by the Idaho legislature or amended by the city council,
and the same is hereby adopted and incorporated as an ordinance of the city as
fully as though set forth at length herein.
   C.   Copy On File: One copy of the Idaho motor vehicle laws, together with
any revisions or amendments, duly certified by the city clerk, shall be kept on
file in the city clerk's office for use and examination by the public. (2004
Code)
5-1-2: MUNICIPAL AUTHORITY:
   A.   Local Traffic Regulations: In all matters relating to traffic control
not covered in the stipulations of this traffic code, the city council shall
have full power to make necessary regulations governing the same. In all points
of dispute as to the interpretation of the stipulations of this code, the city
council's decision shall be final and binding on all parties. (1983 Code §
10.04.040)
   B.   Signs And Signals: The city council has full power to erect or cause to
be erected proper signs or signals on any street or street intersection or at
any railroad crossing directing the method and time of parking, the character
of vehicles allowed to park or stop and directing that vehicles shall stop or
slow down at designated points; or notifying the public of the locations of
schools and hospitals and dangerous street intersections or crossings or of any
other conditions affecting the traffic and control of same. (1983 Code §
10.04.010)
5-1-3: OBEDIENCE TO TRAFFIC OFFICERS:
All persons driving or operating vehicles, riding horseback or walking on the
streets and alleys shall at all times obey the orders, direction and signals of
all traffic officers or city police directing traffic. (1983 Code § 10.04.030)
5-1-4: ONE-WAY STREETS:
The city, acting through its city council, may designate any street or roadway
under its jurisdiction for one-way traffic, and shall cause to be erected
appropriate signs at intersections giving notice thereof. (1983 Code §
10.04.050)
5-1-5: SPEED LIMITS:
   A.   Maximum Limits Set: No person shall drive a vehicle on any side street
within the city at a speed in excess of fifteen (15) miles per hour. (Ord. 320,
9-3-1991)
   B.   Specific Limits:
      1.   The speed limit on the section of highway legally described as state
highway 97 within the city, from where it enters the city at the southwest
boundary to Woodlawn Street shall be forty five (45) miles per hour.
      2.   The speed limit on the section of highway legally described as state
highway 97 within the city, from Woodlawn Street to Yamhill Street (vacated)
shall be thirty five (35) miles per hour.
      3.   The speed limit on the section of highway legally described as state
highway 97 within the city, from Yamhill Street (vacated) to the eastern
boundary of the city shall be twenty five (25) miles per hour. (Ord. 360, 5-1-
2000)
   C.   Penalty  1 : Violation of the provisions of this section shall be an
infraction, and subject to punishment as provided in Idaho Code section 18-
113A. (Ord. 320, 9-3-1991; amd. 2004 Code)
 
Notes
1 1. See subsection
  1-3-1B of this code.
5-1-6: LEAVING VEHICLES UNATTENDED:
No motor propelled vehicle shall be left unattended on any street or alley in
the city while any part of the machinery of said vehicle is in motion. (1983
Code § 10.12.080)
5-1-7: VIOLATION; PENALTY:
Unless otherwise provided in this chapter, any person who disregards or
disobeys or fails to observe any traffic sign or signs regulating traffic
within the city, shall be deemed guilty of a misdemeanor and, upon conviction
thereof, shall be punished as provided in the general penalty in section
1-3-1 of this code. (1983 Code § 10.04.080; amd. 2004 Code)
CHAPTER 2
STOPPING, STANDING AND PARKING
SECTION:
5-2-1: Authority
5-2-2: Parking In Alleys
5-2-3: Municipal Parking Lots
5-2-4: Restricted Parking
5-2-5: Prohibited Parking
5-2-6: Violation; Penalty; Impoundment
5-2-7: Vehicle Ownership As Evidence; Exception
5-2-1: AUTHORITY:
   A.   In all cases where parking regulations are not provided for by
ordinance, the city council shall have power and it is made their duty to
promulgate rules and regulations governing parking of vehicles in the city.
(1983 Code § 10.12.010)
   B.   The city council is empowered to limit the time for which motor
vehicles may be parked within the city and to provide loading and unloading
zones where they deem it expedient and necessary. (1983 Code § 10.12.020)
   C.   It shall be the duty of the city council to have erected suitable signs
and provide striping for streets and alleys where practicable, said signs and
striping to conform to rules and regulations prescribed by the city council.
(1983 Code § 10.12.030)
   D.   The rules and regulations prescribed for the parking of motor vehicles
within the limits of the city shall be subject to the approval of the mayor and
city council by resolution. It shall be the duty of the mayor, after having the
rules and regulations governing parking approved as provided in this chapter,
to file a copy of such rules and regulations in the office of the city clerk.
(Ord. 450, 12-4-2012)
5-2-2: PARKING IN ALLEYS:
The city council shall prescribe the rules and regulations for the parking of
motor vehicles in the alleys of the city, together with rules and regulations
for the parking of motorcycles and bicycles on the streets and in said alleys.
(1983 Code § 10.12.040)
5-2-3: MUNICIPAL PARKING LOTS:
All municipal parking lots within the limits of the city shall be under the
control and supervision of the mayor and city council. (1983 Code § 10.12.050;
amd. 2004 Code)
5-2-4: RESTRICTED PARKING:
   A.   Areas Where Parking Restricted:
      1.   Vehicles On Property Under Control Of The City: It shall be unlawful
for any person to park, place, keep or leave any motor vehicle, piece of
machinery, trailer or equipment on a public street, alley, municipal parking
lot or other public property for any period of time in violation of parking
rules and regulations set by resolution of the city council. (Ord. 450, 12-4-
2012)
      2.   Trailers Or Boats On Streets: It shall be unlawful for any person to
park, place, keep or leave any trailer, boat or nonmotorized vehicle on a
public street, alley or other public property unless attached to a motor
vehicle capable of towing said trailer, boat or nonmotorized vehicle.
      3.   Vehicles On Street Without Current License: It shall be unlawful for
any person to place, keep or leave any motor vehicle, piece of machinery,
trailer or equipment on a public street, alley or other public property that
does not display current, lawful license and tags.
      4.   Wrecked Or Partially Dismantled Vehicles: It shall be unlawful to
keep or leave any motor vehicle, piece of machinery, trailer or equipment that
is in an inoperable condition or in a wrecked or partially dismantled condition
or in a state of repair for a period of forty eight (48) hours or more on a
public street, alley or other public property.
      5.   Vehicles On Private Property: It shall be unlawful for any person to
place, keep or leave any motor vehicle, piece of machinery, trailer or
equipment in a wrecked or partially dismantled condition or in a state of
disrepair for a period of more than ten (10) days on private property unless
enclosed in a building or other area screened from public view and fenced in a
manner to prevent children from entering the property. Any such fence and
screening shall be constructed in compliance with the current provisions of the
international building code. Such vehicle, machinery, trailer or equipment is
hereby declared to be a public nuisance unless properly fenced or enclosed.
      6.   Vehicles Or Equipment Causing Environmental Concerns: It shall be
unlawful for any person to place, keep or leave any motor vehicle, piece of
equipment or machinery in a fashion which permits same to leak or discharge oil
or gasoline onto the ground or pavement or which discharges freon into the air.
Similarly, it shall be unlawful for any person to dump, discharge or in any
manner dispose of oil, gasoline or hazardous chemical waste on any public
street, alley, other public property and private property not zoned for such
use.
      7.   Unauthorized Vehicles In Designated Disabled Spaces: It shall be
unlawful for any vehicle to be parked in a designated disabled parking space
without bearing license plates, signs or shields identifying the owner of such
vehicle as having a disability. The city council shall approve the location of
such spaces by resolution. This provision shall be in compliance with Idaho
Code 49-213.
      8.   Snow Emergency Routes: Whenever the mayor finds, on the basis of
falling snow, sleet or freezing rain, that weather conditions will make it
necessary that motor vehicle traffic be expedited and that parking on city
streets be prohibited or restricted for snow plowing and other purposes, he
shall put into effect a parking prohibition on primary snow emergency routes as
necessary. "Primary snow emergency routes" are defined as those streets
generally traversing the entire city or a major part thereof that are
considered essential to the rapid movement of emergency vehicles and normally
carry the heaviest traffic volumes.
      9.   Construction Or Street Sweeping: Whenever the mayor finds it
necessary that parking on city streets be prohibited or restricted for the
purposes of street or utility construction or repair or for street sweeping or
cleaning, he shall put into effect, with twelve (12) hours prior posted notice,
a parking prohibition on the affected streets.
   B.   Signs For Restricted Parking: The mayor and city council have authority
to designate city staff to erect signage designating disabled parking spaces
and any other restricted or limited parking as is deemed necessary. Application
of this provision shall be in compliance with Idaho Code. (Ord. 374, 4-12-2001;
amd. 2004 Code)
5-2-5: PROHIBITED PARKING:
Parking of motor vehicles is hereby prohibited in the following places and
under the following circumstances:
   A.   No vehicles shall be parked within twelve feet (12') of street
intersections. (1983 Code § 10.12.090; amd. 2004 Code)
5-2-6: VIOLATION; PENALTY; IMPOUNDMENT:
   A.   Violation of the provisions of this chapter shall be an infraction as
provided in subsection
1-3-1B of this code.
   B.   In addition to or in lieu of any infraction penalty, any law
enforcement officer or other person designated by the city may issue a civil
citation. The civil assessment shall be twenty five dollars ($25.00) to be paid
to the city. The civil citation assessment shall be payable at city hall within
thirty (30) days from the date of issuance. If the civil penalty is paid within
thirty (30) days from the date of the issuance of the civil assessment, the
civil penalty will be reduced to ten dollars ($10.00). No partial payments will
be accepted as full payment. If, within the thirty (30) day period following
the issuance of the city civil citation the assessment has not been paid, an
infraction uniform citation or sworn complaint may be issued for the violation
of this chapter or the rules, and the violator, if found guilty, will be fined
in the amount of twenty five dollars ($25.00) for the violation plus court
costs. Nothing contained herein prohibits a law enforcement officer from
issuance of a uniform infraction citation instead of a civil citation.
   C.   The sheriff's department is authorized, in its discretion, to remove
and impound at such place as may be designated by the sheriff's department any
vehicle, piece of machinery, trailer or equipment which is parked in violation
of any provision of this chapter. All costs and expenses of taking and keeping
such vehicle, including the costs and expenses of towing, keeping and storing,
shall be paid by the owner of such vehicle and shall constitute a lien upon
such vehicle. (Ord. 455, 5-6-2014)
5-2-7: VEHICLE OWNERSHIP AS EVIDENCE; EXCEPTION:
   A.   In any prosecution against the registered owner of a motor vehicle
charging a violation of any regulation governing the standing or parking of a
vehicle under any ordinance of the city, proof that the particular vehicle
described in the complaint was parked in violation of any such ordinance,
together with proof that the defendant named in the complaint was, at the time
of parking, the registered owner of the vehicle, shall constitute prima facie
evidence that the registered owner of the vehicle was the person who parked or
placed the vehicle at the point where, and for the time during which, the
violation occurred. For the purposes of this subsection, proof that a person is
the registered owner of a vehicle is not prima facie evidence that the
registered owner has violated any other provision of law. Proof of a written
lease or of a rental agreement for a particular vehicle described in the
complaint on the date and time of the violation, which lease or rental
agreement includes the name and address of the person to whom the vehicle is
leased or rented, shall rebut the prima facie evidence that the registered
owner was the person who parked or placed the vehicle at the time and place
where the violations occurred.
   B.   In any prosecution against the lessee or renter of a motor vehicle
charging a violation of any regulation governing the standing or parking of a
vehicle under any ordinance of the city, proof that the particular vehicle
described in the complaint was parked in violation of any provision of the
ordinance, together with proof that the defendant named in the complaint was,
at the time of parking, the lessee or renter of the vehicle, shall constitute
prima facie evidence that the lessee or renter of the vehicle was the person
who parked the vehicle at the point where, and for the time during which, the
violation occurred. For the purposes of this subsection, proof that a person is
the lessee or renter of a vehicle is not prima facie evidence that the lessee
or renter has violated any other provision of this law.
   C.   Any charge under such ordinance shall be dismissed when the person
charged has made a bona fide sale or transfer of the vehicle, has delivered
possession thereof to the purchaser, and has complied with the requirements of
Idaho Code title 49, chapter 4, prior to the date of the alleged violation and
has advised the court of the name and address of the purchaser and the date of
the sale. (Ord. 455, 5-6-2014)
CHAPTER 3
SNOWMOBILES
SECTION:
5-3-1: Operation On Public Streets And Highways
5-3-2: Operating Requirements
5-3-3: Violation; Penalty
5-3-1: OPERATION ON PUBLIC STREETS AND HIGHWAYS:
   A.   City Streets: It is unlawful for any owner or operator of any snow
vehicle, commonly known as a snowmobile to operate the same along or upon any
city street, alley or thoroughfare except under the following conditions:
      1.   Such snowmobiles may be used on the city streets only for the
limited purpose of transporting the same from one section of town to another,
or to a field or other designated area where the same may be operated, and said
transportation must be along the shortest feasible route. Such vehicles are not
to be used for pleasure or for general operation on the city streets at any
time.
      2.   No snowmobile may be operated upon or along any city street after
nine o'clock (9:00) P.M., with the exception that such operation may be
permitted after the nine o'clock (9:00) P.M. curfew for the sole and limited
purpose of transporting such vehicle directly to the home of the owner or
operator thereof, and for no other purpose. (1983 Code § 10.08.010)
   B.   State Highway 97: No snowmobiles may be operated on state highway 97
within the city limits, this being a highway as opposed to city streets of the
city. (1983 Code § 10.08.050)
5-3-2: OPERATING REQUIREMENTS:
   A.   Single File: All snowmobiles operating on the city streets must travel
single file, and there must be not less than a fifty foot (50') interval
between two (2) or more vehicles operating on said streets.
   B.   Speed Limits: The speed limit shall not exceed ten (10) miles per hour.
   C.   Obey Traffic Laws: All vehicles operating upon the city streets must
stop at all intersections and obey all applicable state, county and motor
vehicle laws. (1983 Code § 10.08.020; amd. 2004 Code)
   D.   Equipment: All vehicles operated on the city streets for the limited
purposes herein permitted shall have qualified and properly functioning
mufflers, and must be properly lighted. (1983 Code § 10.08.030)
   E.   Valid Driver's License: All operators of snowmobiles within the city
and under the terms and provisions of this chapter shall have in effect and in
their possession a valid state of Idaho driver's license. (1983 Code §
10.08.040)
5-3-3: VIOLATION; PENALTY:
Any person violating the provisions of this chapter shall be deemed guilty of a
misdemeanor and, upon conviction thereof may be punished as provided in the
general penalty in section
1-3-1 of this code. (1983 Code § 10.08.060; amd. 2004 Code)
TITLE 6
PUBLIC WAYS AND PROPERTY
CHAPTER 1
STREETS AND PUBLIC WAYS
SECTION:
6-1-1: Municipal Authority
6-1-2: Street Improvements
6-1-3: City Base And Grades Established
6-1-4: Use Of Public Ways
6-1-5: Obstructions
6-1-6: Trees Overhanging Public Ways
6-1-7: Encroachments
6-1-8: Excavations
6-1-9: Liability For Damages
6-1-10: Violation; Penalty
6-1-1: MUNICIPAL AUTHORITY:
All streets, alleys and public thoroughfares in the city shall be under the
immediate supervision of the mayor. He shall be in charge subject to the orders
of the city council. (1983 Code § 12.04.010)
6-1-2: STREET IMPROVEMENTS:
No new permanent improvement shall be undertaken by the mayor except upon the
order and direction of the city council. (1983 Code § 12.04.020)
6-1-3: CITY BASE AND GRADES ESTABLISHED:
   A.   Base: A city base is fixed and established at the south quarter corner
of section 6, township 47 north, range 3, west Boise Meridian, said point also
being the 291/2 mile corner of the new north boundary of the Coeur d'Alene
Indian reservation. All official grades and elevations fixed and established on
any of the streets and avenues and sidewalks of the city shall be with
reference to and computed from the city base as fixed and established in this
subsection. (1983 Code § 12.04.150)
   B.   Grade Lines: All grades and lines shall be established and approved by
the city council in accordance with ordinances establishing the grade lines of
the various streets and curbs. (1983 Code § 12.04.160)
6-1-4: USE OF PUBLIC WAYS:
   A.   Heavy Equipment And Loads:
      1.   It is prohibited and made unlawful for any person to drag, push,
pull or otherwise propel any poles, logs, ties, boards or other pieces of
timber or heavy materials over any graded or otherwise improved streets within
the city. (1983 Code § 12.04.030)
      2.   It is prohibited and made unlawful for any person to drive, drag,
pull, push or otherwise propel over or upon any graded or otherwise improved
street within the city; or cause to be driven, dragged, pulled, pushed or
propelled over any improved streets of the city, any vehicle having a gross
weight being the combined weight of the vehicle plus accessories plus load of
more than three hundred (300) pounds per inch width of tire (both pneumatic and
solid) on any one wheel concentrated on the surface of the roadway, such width
being determined by the manufacturer's rated width thereof; any vehicle or
machine having lugged tires or treads, or any heavy vehicle, machine or thing
which will be destructive to, or tend to interfere with or injure, the surface,
base or any part of such street of the city. Each separate act of driving,
dragging, pulling, pushing or propelling in violation of this section shall
constitute a separate violation hereof; and any person convicted of violating
this section shall be punished as provided in the general penalty in section
1-3-1 of this code for each violation. (1983 Code § 12.04.040; amd. 2004 Code)
   B.   Waiver Of Weight Limitations: Upon written request being made to the
city council at any regular meeting or special meeting called for that purpose,
any person desiring to transport loads in excess of the limitation set forth in
subsection A of this section, may make written application to the city council
for waiver of said limitations, said written application to be submitted to the
city clerk not less than twenty four (24) hours prior to the next regularly
scheduled meeting of the city council. Said written application shall specify
the dates upon which waiver is requested, the reasons therefor, a statement of
the loads and weights thereof anticipated to be carried on such dates, the
route to be followed along the city streets and a statement of precautions
which are to be taken to protect the roads, the utility lines and the health,
welfare and safety of the residents of the city. The burden of proof as to the
exceptional need for such waiver and that such need overrides in importance the
threat to the streets, the utilities and the residents of the city shall lie
with the applicant, and the decision of the city council on such matters shall
be final. In the event that the city shall grant a waiver, such waiver shall be
limited to the dates, times and conditions set forth in such waiver, including
the condition of the posting of a bond by the applicant to ensure payment of
any and all damages accruing as a result of such waiver. The applicant's
failure to conform the activities authorized thereby to the terms and
conditions specified in the waiver shall constitute a misdemeanor, each
enumerated term or condition thereof violated constituting a separate offense;
and any person convicted of violating this subsection shall be punished as
provided in the general penalty in section
1-3-1 of this code. (1983 Code § 12.04.042)
   C.   Driving Vehicles Over Curbs: It is prohibited and made unlawful for any
person to back, push or otherwise propel any auto, truck, wagon or any vehicle
of any nature whatsoever over or across any curb on any of the streets and
avenues of the city, or cause the same to be done, other than in a place
specially provided for each purpose and, if so provided, it must be done
pursuant to the rules of the city supervisor and approved by him. (1983 Code §
12.04.050)
6-1-5: OBSTRUCTIONS:
   A.   Gutters And Pipes: It is unlawful for any person to obstruct any of the
gutters on any street within the city, or to obstruct any artificial carrier or
conductor of any surface waters; or to, in any manner, obstruct any pipe,
drain, sewer or other carrier or conductor of surface waters or sewerage
whether above or underneath any street or property within the city by placing
thereon or therein any dirt, refuse, snow, ice or any other matter or thing
which shall in any manner prevent the free discharge and drainage of water
through, over or in such gutters, pipes or other carriers or drains. (1983 Code
§ 12.04.070)
   B.   Streets: It is unlawful for any person to in any manner obstruct any of
the streets or avenues within the city by placing or leaving thereon any brick,
rock or any other material which will have a tendency to obstruct or blockade
the free use of such streets or avenues; provided, however, that nothing herein
contained shall prevent the city council or the street and alley committee of
the city from authorizing the use of such portions of any street or avenue as
may be necessary for the piling of lumber and building material to be used in
the actual construction of buildings, or in the repair or alteration of
existing buildings. (1983 Code § 12.04.080)
6-1-6: TREES OVERHANGING PUBLIC WAYS:
All shade trees, including fruit bearing trees, located within the boundaries
of a dedicated street or alley, shall have all foliage, including leaves and
branches, trimmed up to a point seven feet (7') above the level of the sidewalk
under or near said trees, and if there is no sidewalk, to a point fourteen feet
(14') above the average level of the traveled roadway opposite said trees.
(1983 Code § 10.04.020; amd. 2004 Code)
6-1-7: ENCROACHMENTS:
   A.   Prohibited: It shall be unlawful for any person to use any part of the
public streets, highways, rights of ways or alleys within the city, or to in
any manner encroach thereon for the purpose of displaying, selling or
dispensing any merchandise or goods, or placing of any advertising signs, gas
pumps, structures, fences or any other encroachments, including the storage of
machinery, materials, equipment, junk or any other personally owned property.
(1983 Code § 12.04.090)
   B.   Exceptions; Permit Required: Any person desiring to use any highway,
street, or alley or any part thereof, for any private purpose, must apply in
writing; and upon city council approval, the city clerk shall issue a permit
allowing the encroachment; and provided further, that the proposed encroachment
will not operate to the detriment to the city, or the residents and citizens
and users of said streets, highways or alleys therein. (1983 Code § 12.04.100)
6-1-8: EXCAVATIONS:
   A.   Permit Required: It is unlawful for any person to break up, dig up, cut
up, excavate, fill in, do any work upon or in any way whatsoever interfere
with, any street, alley, avenue, lane, sidewalk, crosswalk or other public
improvement or pavement without having first obtained a permit therefor as
provided in this section.
   B.   Application And Fee: Application for an excavation permit shall be
filed with the city clerk and shall specify the kind and location of the
proposed work, the time when the same shall begin, and the time when the same
shall be completed, which time shall in no case exceed thirty (30) days unless
a renewal of such permit is granted by the city council. The mayor may impose
such conditions as may be necessary to ensure that the city and residents be
protected. The applicant shall pay an application fee and any other fees
associated with the excavation permit at the time of issuance of the permit.
The fees shall be set by resolution of the city council.
   C.   Supervision Of Work: It shall be the duty of the mayor to supervise the
filling in of any excavation above set forth and the resurfacing of such
street, alley, avenue, lane, sidewalk or crosswalk, and he shall see that such
work is done in conformity with the type of surfacing upon the balance of
street, alley, lane, avenue or crosswalk.
   D.   Liability For Damages: The person upon whose application the work is
done shall assume all liability and responsibility for the costs involved and
for any injury or damages that might result from the excavation, cutting or
other work involved. (Ord. 410, 7-11-2006)
6-1-9: LIABILITY FOR DAMAGES:
In addition to any fine or other penalty which may be incurred as a result of
the violation of any of the provisions of this chapter, and whether or not
criminal charges shall be brought with regard to any such violation and without
regard to the determination of guilt or innocence if any such charges are
pressed, any person violating any provision of this chapter shall be civilly
liable to the city for all damages incurred as a result of such violation,
including damages to streets, sidewalks and utility lines, and any other
property of the city. (1983 Code § 12.04.175)
6-1-10: VIOLATION; PENALTY:
Any person violating any of the provisions of this chapter shall be guilty of a
misdemeanor and, upon conviction, shall be punished as provided in the general
penalty in section
1-3-1 of this code. (1983 Code § 12.04.170)
CHAPTER 2
STREET VACATIONS
SECTION:
6-2-1: Application For Vacation
6-2-2: Objections
6-2-3: Hearing Procedures
6-2-4: Damage Assessments
6-2-5: Plat Requirements
6-2-1: APPLICATION FOR VACATION:
Any person owning any interest in real estate abutting on any street, avenue or
public way, who may desire the vacation of such street, avenue or public way,
or any part thereof, may make application therefor by causing to be filed with
the city clerk a petition therefor giving a description of the property to be
vacated; and thereupon the city council may, and if such petition is signed by
the owners of a majority of the private property abutting upon that part of
such street, avenue or public way, shall, by resolution, fix a time when said
petition shall be heard, which time shall be not more than forty (40) nor less
than ten (10) days from the date of the passage of such resolution; and upon
the passage of such resolution it shall be the duty of the petitioner to give
seven (7) days' notice of the pending of such application by written or printed
notice posted in three (3) public places in the city, one of which shall be
posted in a conspicuous place on or adjacent to the street, avenue or public
way sought to be vacated, and by causing such notice to be published once, not
less than one week prior to the hearing of said application, in the official
newspaper of the city. Such notice shall contain a statement that a petition
has been filed to vacate the street, avenue or public way, or the portion
thereof sought to be vacated, describing the property to be vacated together
with a statement of the time and place fixed for the hearing of said petition.
(1983 Code § 12.08.010; amd. 2004 Code)
6-2-2: OBJECTIONS:
Any person claiming to be injured by such vacation shall, at or before the time
fixed for such hearing, file, in writing and with the city clerk, his
objections thereto setting forth the grounds of such objections, describing the
property which he claims will be injured by such vacation, and setting forth
the nature and extent of such injury and the amount of damages claimed; and
such person failing to so file such objections shall be deemed to have waived
all claims for damages for or on account of such vacation. (1983 Code §
12.08.020)
6-2-3: HEARING PROCEDURES:
At the time appointed for hearing such petition, or at the time to which such
hearing may be adjourned by the mayor and city council, the mayor and city
council shall consider the said petition, and all objections filed thereto, and
shall hear the said parties; provided it shall then appear to the satisfaction
of the mayor and city council that notice of said hearing has been given as
herein provided, and in the event that such body shall determine to grant the
prayer of said petition, the mayor and city council shall thereupon, by
ordinance, vacate such street, avenue, public way or portion thereof. (1983
Code § 12.08.030)
6-2-4: DAMAGE ASSESSMENTS:
In the event that it shall be determined to vacate such street, avenue, public
way or portion thereof, and if any claim or claims for damages by reason
thereof shall have been filed as provided in section
6-2-3 of this chapter, the mayor shall appoint five (5) disinterested persons
who shall, before the passage of such vacation ordinance, assess and determine
what, if any, damage will be caused to the property of each objector and shall
immediately file with the city clerk a report of their findings stating the
amount of each item of damage. (1983 Code § 12.08.040)
6-2-5: PLAT REQUIREMENTS:
Any person seeking the vacation of any street or alley, or any portion of any
street or alley, within the city shall file with his petition and application
for vacation a plat designating and showing that portion of the street or alley
sought to be vacated. Said plat shall be duly certified to by a licensed
engineer. In the event that the said street or alley is vacated by order of the
city council, the applicant, upon the passage of an ordinance vacating any
street or alley, or any portion of any street or alley, shall file said plat
showing the streets or alleys, or portions of such streets or alleys, vacated
with the county recorder of Kootenai County; and said ordinance shall not
become effective until a certificate of the county recorder of Kootenai County,
has been filed with the city clerk showing that the plat therein mentioned has
been duly recorded in his office. (1983 Code § 12.08.050)
CHAPTER 3
SIDEWALKS
SECTION:
6-3-1: Material Specifications
6-3-2: Grades And Specifications
6-3-3: Costs Of Construction
6-3-4: Construction Procedures
6-3-5: Liens
6-3-6: Snow Removal
6-3-7: Prohibited Acts And Conditions
6-3-8: Violation; Penalty
6-3-1: MATERIAL SPECIFICATIONS:
   A.   Mayor's Authority: All sidewalks built or constructed within the city
limits shall be constructed of cement or material pursuant to specifications of
the mayor. (1983 Code § 12.12.010)
   B.   Plank Or Wooden Sidewalks: It is unlawful for any person, either
directly or indirectly, to construct along his property or to allow to be
constructed any plank, board or wood sidewalk within the city limits without
first having secured a permit from the mayor and city council to do so. (1983
Code § 12.12.020)
6-3-2: GRADES AND SPECIFICATIONS:
All sidewalks built or ordered to be built within the city shall be built and
constructed upon the grades heretofore or hereafter established; provided,
however, that the city council may order sidewalks to conform to the surface of
the ground where the streets have not been graded, and provided further that
such order shall not establish the grade of such sidewalk nor shall the city be
liable for any damage thereto by reason of the grading of any streets where
such temporary sidewalks have been constructed in accordance with this section.
All sidewalks constructed hereafter in any residential district shall be forty
inches (40") in width and constructed integral with or abutting the curb if
then constructed or then being constructed. If the curb is not then
constructed, the sidewalk shall be laid to what will be the inside line of the
curb when constructed. (1983 Code § 12.12.110; amd. 2004 Code)
6-3-3: COSTS OF CONSTRUCTION:
   A.   Owner Liable For Costs: All sidewalks upon any street, avenue or
highway within the city shall be constructed and maintained by the property
owner owning the land in front of which such sidewalk shall be constructed,
repaired or maintained. The property owner shall be liable for all costs, and
the costs of such construction, maintenance or repair is made a first lien upon
said lots or lands fronting or abutting any streets, avenues or highways upon
which any construction, maintenance or repair is done. (1983 Code § 12.12.030)
   B.   Construction By City: All sidewalks shall be built by the owner or
owners of the property adjacent thereto or abutting thereon, but if built by
the city, the costs of construction shall be charged to the lots or land
fronting or abutting thereon or adjacent thereto as shall the costs of repair
or maintenance thereon; provided, however, that the city council may, in cases
where they deem it proper, construct or repair any sidewalks within the city
and charge the same to the property or lots as provided in this section. (1983
Code § 12.12.040)
6-3-4: CONSTRUCTION PROCEDURES:
   A.   Order Of City: Whenever the city council or mayor shall deem it
necessary, they shall order sidewalks to be constructed, repaired, replaced or
built upon and along any street or avenue or highway and in front of any lot,
piece or parcel of land fronting or abutting upon such street, avenue or
highway. Such order shall be made by resolution and be shown upon the minutes
of the city council. If such order is to build a sidewalk of different
dimensions or of different material than the general rules of the city require,
the said resolution shall specifically state the kind and character of such
sidewalk, its dimensions and the mode of its construction. (1983 Code §
12.12.050)
   B.   Notice Required: Notice of the proposed action shall be given by the
city council at least ten (10) days prior to the time the proposed action is to
be taken. The notice must be given personally to the property owner or owners
upon whose property the proposed sidewalks are to be constructed or, if the
owner or owners live without the state or, after reasonable search, cannot be
found within the state, the notice shall be published in one issue of the
official newspaper of the city and a copy of the notice mailed to the last
known address of the property owner or owners. If an agent of the owner who
cannot be found resides upon the property or in the state, notice shall also be
sent to said agent. (1983 Code § 12.12.060)
   C.   Hearing: The property owner or owners shall be given an opportunity to
be heard in person or by attorney at the meeting at which the proposed action
is to be taken and may present evidence in opposition thereto. The judicial
rules of evidence shall not be applicable and the hearing shall be informal and
shall be conducted as provided in section
1-9-2 of this code. The city council shall determine whether it is in the best
interest of the city that such proposed action be taken. At such hearing, the
city council may revise, reform or correct the proposed resolution and approve
the same as corrected. The resolution and order shall be subject to an appeal
to the courts within twenty (20) days after final action thereon and not
thereafter. (1983 Code § 12.12.070; amd. 2004 Code)
   D.   Time Limits: The order of the city council shall be that the owner or
owners shall within five (5) days begin construction of the sidewalks required
and, if he fails to do so or fails to complete the sidewalks within a
reasonable time, not in excess of thirty (30) days, the mayor, without further
authority from the city council, shall proceed to construct the same and shall
keep an account of the cost and expense thereof and at the next regular or
special meeting of the city council shall submit a copy to the city council by
filing the same with the city clerk and, if the city council shall approve the
cost, the same shall be and is a first lien against such lot, piece or parcel
of land which fronts or abuts upon the sidewalk constructed and shall be
charged thereto and steps to collect the same shall be taken by the city
attorney. (1983 Code § 12.12.080)
6-3-5: LIENS:
   A.   Lien Against Adjacent Property  1 : The costs of construction, repair
or maintenance of all sidewalks constructed pursuant to this chapter shall be a
first lien upon the land fronting or abutting upon the sidewalks so
constructed, repaired or maintained and the same shall be certified to the
county. The lien may be collected by foreclosure proceedings by suit brought in
the name of the city. All monies due the city for the construction, repair or
maintenance of any sidewalk upon which the work is done by the city are due,
owing and payable within ten (10) days after the construction, repair or
maintenance of such sidewalk, and the sum shall bear interest from that date at
the prevailing statutory rate until paid. (1983 Code § 12.12.090)
   B.   Notice; Hearing; Appeal: Within five (5) days after entering such
liens, the city clerk shall mail a notice of the total amount of the lien,
together with a description of the property to the owner of the property at his
last known address or, if the owner is not known, to his agent or, if no agent
is known, to the tenant or occupant of the premises or, if there is no such
occupant, then by publication in one issue of the official newspaper of the
city. Within ten (10) days after the mailing or publication of such notice, any
party interested may file with the city clerk a written protest against such
assessment. If a protest is made, the city council shall fix a time and place
for hearing the same, give reasonable notice of such hearing to the party
protesting, and may, upon such hearing, approve the assessment, or revise,
reform or correct the assessment and approve the same as corrected. The hearing
provided shall be in accordance with the provisions of section
1-9-2 of this code, and the city council shall determine whether the assessment
upon the property is reasonable in relation to the properties in close
proximity thereto. If no protest is made, the assessment shall be deemed
automatically approved and confirming any assessment hereunder shall be subject
to an appeal to the courts within twenty (20) days from the date of the final
order and no appeal shall lie thereafter. (1983 Code § 12.12.100; amd. 2004
Code)
 
Notes
1 1. IC § 45-101 et seq.
6-3-6: SNOW REMOVAL:
