   A.   Removal Of Snow And Ice Required: Every person who may own, lease or
occupy any building within the corporate limits of the city which abuts on any
street of the city and has a sidewalk in front of said building, shall clean
the same of any snow, slush, ice or other refuse within ten (10) hours after
any storm that may take place.
   B.   Failure To Remove Snow Or Ice: Any person who neglects to comply with
the provisions of this section shall be deemed guilty of an offense, and upon
conviction shall be fined as provided in the general penalty in section
1-3-1 of this code. (2004 Code)
6-3-7: PROHIBITED ACTS AND CONDITIONS:
   A.   Coasting, Riding Or Sledding: It shall be unlawful for any person upon
roller skates, rollerblades, inline skates, or riding any coaster, toy vehicle
or similar device, to be upon any roadway except while crossing a street within
a crosswalk; and when crossing, such person shall be granted all the rights and
shall be subject to all of the duties applicable to pedestrians. (1983 Code §
12.12.120; amd. 2004 Code)
   B.   Driving On Sidewalks: It is unlawful for any person to drive or cause
to be driven any wagon, automobile, truck or any other vehicle of any kind or
nature across any of the sidewalks of the city other than at a place specially
constructed for such purpose. (1983 Code § 12.12.130)
   C.   Bicycles On Sidewalks: It shall be unlawful for any person to park,
ride or propel any bicycle upon the sidewalks of the city within the business
district or any other congested district of the city that may be so designated
by proclamation of the mayor. (2004 Code)
6-3-8: VIOLATION; PENALTY:
Any person violating any of the provisions of this chapter shall be deemed
guilty of a misdemeanor and, upon conviction thereof, shall be punished as
provided in the general penalty in section
1-3-1 of this code. (1983 Code § 12.12.140)
CHAPTER 4
PUBLIC IMPROVEMENTS
SECTION:
6-4-1: Public Improvement Requirements
6-4-2: Water Facilities
6-4-3: Sewer Facilities
6-4-4: Underground Utilities
6-4-5: Streets And Sidewalks
6-4-6: Stormwater Facilities
6-4-7: Off Street Parking
6-4-8: Violations; Penalty
6-4-1: PUBLIC IMPROVEMENT REQUIREMENTS:
   A.   Street, Water And Sewer Extensions:
      1.   Any owner seeking to develop property within the city or seeking
connection to the city water or sewer system shall be responsible for paying
for the extension of such facilities, including streets and stormwater
facilities, to the property.
      2.   All utility and street extensions shall be designed by a licensed
engineer. Plans must be approved by the city prior to construction and as built
plans shall be provided to the city. Such extensions shall be made in
accordance with all city and state standards including fire hydrants and
manholes.
      3.   The city may require that water and sewer lines be sized to provide
services beyond the needs of the property being developed. In such case, the
city shall pay the incremental costs related to increasing the size of the
line.
   B.   Approval Of Plans; Engineering Costs: Plans for all improvements must
meet all specifications of this chapter brought to and approved by the city
council before any work is done. Within thirty (30) days of completion of
construction, as built plans shall be provided to the city. The owner shall
reimburse the city for all engineering costs incurred by the city.
   C.   Inspection By City: No water line, sewer line or stormwater pipe shall
be covered until it has been inspected by the city. The developer or contractor
shall provide at least twenty four (24) hours' notice to city of need for
inspection. All public facilities shall be warranted by the developer or
contractor for a period of three (3) years after acceptance by the city. (Ord.
362, 3-7-2000)
6-4-2: WATER FACILITIES:
Water lines within the city shall comply with the following standards:
   A.   All work shall conform to the "Idaho Standards For Public Works
Construction" (ISPWC), current edition, and the city of Harrison standards and
specifications. In the case of conflict, the most stringent standard shall
apply. (Ord. 422, 12-4-2007)
   B.   Fire hydrants shall be constructed every four hundred feet (400').
   C.   All plans shall be subject to approval by the city engineer. (Ord. 362,
3-7-2000)
6-4-3: SEWER FACILITIES:
Sewer lines shall comply with the following standards:
   A.   All work shall conform to the "Idaho Standards For Public Works
Construction" (ISPWC), current edition, and the city of Harrison standards and
specifications. In the case of conflict, the most stringent standard shall
apply. (Ord. 422, 12-4-2007)
   B.   All plans shall be subject to approval by the city engineer. (Ord. 362,
3-7-2000)
6-4-4: UNDERGROUND UTILITIES:
   A.   Whenever in this section the words or phrases hereinafter defined are
used, they shall have the following definitions:
   COMMISSION: The public utilities commission of the state.
   POLES, OVERHEAD WIRES AND ASSOCIATED STRUCTURES: Poles, towers, supports,
wires, conductors, guys, stubs, platforms, crossarms, braces, transformers,
insulators, cutouts, switches, communication circuits, appliances, attachments
and appurtenances located above ground within the city and used or useful in
supplying electric, communication or similar or associated service.
   B.   All wires and facilities for supplying electric, communication, data
transmission or similar or associated service within the city installed after
the effective date of this chapter shall be installed underground.
   C.   This chapter does not apply to all poles, overhead wires and associated
overhead structures within the city which exist and have been installed prior
to the adoption of this chapter; the section does apply to wires and facilities
which undergo replacement or a substantial renovation.
   D.   After the effective date of this chapter, it shall be unlawful for any
person or utility to erect, construct, maintain, employ or operate poles,
overhead wires and associated overhead structures in the city unless otherwise
provided for in subsection E or F of this section.
   E.   This section does not apply to the following types of facilities:
      1.   Overhead facilities installed and maintained, without authority of
the city engineer, to provide emergency service for a period not to exceed ten
(10) days.
      2.   Cases of emergency where the city engineer grants special
permission, without discrimination as to any person or utility, to erect,
construct, install, maintain, use or operate poles, overhead wires and
associated overhead structures.
      3.   Poles and lamps used exclusively for street lighting.
      4.   Overhead wires, exclusive of supporting structures, crossing through
the city when such wires originate in an area from which poles, overhead wires
and associated structures are not prohibited.
      5.   Overhead wires attached to the exterior surface of a building by
means of a bracket or other fixture and extending from one location on the
building to another location on the same building or extending from the
building to another building without crossing any public street.
      6.   Antennas, associated equipment and supporting structures, used by a
utility for furnishing communication services.
      7.   Temporary poles, overhead wires and associated overhead structures
used or to be used in conjunction with construction projects.
   F.   Any person or utility may petition the city for a variance to erect,
construct, install, maintain, use or operate poles, overhead wires and
associated overhead structures, notwithstanding the provisions of this chapter.
The city will utilize its variance procedures, established pursuant the local
planning act 1 , to decide such requests.
   G.   If underground construction is necessary to provide utility service
within the city, the supplying utility shall furnish that portion of the
conduits, conductors and associated equipment required to be furnished by it
under applicable rules, regulations and tariffs on file with the commission;
provided, that if any provision of any franchise agreement between the city and
the supplying utility is clearly in conflict with any provision of this
section, the provision of the franchise agreement shall prevail. (Ord. 362, 3-
7-2000)
 
Notes
1 1. See title 9, chapter 10 of this code.
6-4-5: STREETS AND SIDEWALKS:
Rights of way and sidewalks shall be constructed to the requirements of this
section. Dedication of streets to these standards shall be a condition of
development unless waived by the city council.
   A.   Minimum Standards: All streets and sidewalks shall be to the following
minimum standards:
      1.   Streets:
         a.   Base of at least twelve inches (12") (minimum) of rock with at
least six inches (6") (pit run not smaller than 3 inch diameter) topped by at
least four inches (4") of one and one-quarter inch (11/4") crushed aggregate,
graded and finished with an additional surface of at least two inches (2") of
crushed aggregate three-quarter inch (3/4"). This surface shall be
appropriately compacted to meet current engineering standards.
         b.   The driving surface shall be paved with asphalt on the above
indicated compacted base at located in the center of road unless otherwise
located by the city engineer.
      2.   Curbs: Curbs shall be constructed on both sides of the street unless
waived by the city council.
      3.   Sidewalks: Sidewalks shall be at least forty inches (40") in width
and shall be constructed of concrete four inches (4") in depth (6 inches at
curb cuts and driveways) with at least four inches (4") of compacted gravel as
a base. A sidewalk shall be developed on one side of the street in single-
family residential areas and on both sides in commercial, industrial and multi-
family residential areas. Expansion joints shall be located at least every
thirty feet (30'), and scribed lines every forty inches (40") or to match the
width of the sidewalk.
      4.   Alternative Materials: The city council may permit alternate
materials or, where it is in the public interest, permit installations to be
delayed until adjacent properties develop.
   B.   Residential Streets (Local Access Road):
      1.   Dedicated right of way shall be fifty feet (50') in width with a
five foot (5') utility easement on each side. Width of surfacing and usable
shoulders shall be at least forty feet (40').
      2.   The street shall be constructed to at least thirty feet (30') in
width with asphalt of at least two and one-half inches (2 1/2") thick on the
above indicated compacted base at least twenty feet (20') in width placed as
designated by the city engineer.
   C.   Minor Collector Streets:
      1.   Dedicated right of way shall be fifty feet (50') in width.
      2.   The street shall be constructed to at least forty feet (40') in
width (travel width of at least 22 feet and 9 foot wide parking lane on each
side). The travelway shall be finished with asphalt at least four inches (4")
thick.
      3.   The following streets are minor collectors: (reserved)
   D.   Major Collectors:
      1.   Dedicated right of way shall be eighty feet (80') in width with a
five foot (5') utility easement on each side.
      2.   The street shall be constructed to at least forty four feet (44') in
width (24 foot travel lanes with 10 foot parking on each side) with asphalt at
least four inches (4") thick with a paved width of at least twenty four feet
(24').
      3.   Sidewalks with a minimum width of five feet (5') shall be developed
on both sides of the street.
      4.   The following streets are hereby designated as major collectors:
(reserved). (Ord. 362, 3-7-2000)
6-4-6: STORMWATER FACILITIES:
Stormwater facilities shall be installed at the time of or prior to development
of adjacent property. Stormwater facilities must be designed by a civil
engineer. If a project will place a burden on downstream facilities, the
developer may be required to construct or improve such off site facilities. The
city may waive the requirement of an engineered design for a small project upon
a determination by the council that the complexity of the project does not
require engineered plans. For purposes of this section, small projects are less
than two (2) acres in size and one hundred thousand dollars ($100,000.00) in
construction costs. All subdivisions must have engineered plans for
improvements 1 . (Ord. 362, 3-7-2000)
 
Notes
1 1. See title 10 of this code.
6-4-7: OFF STREET PARKING:
Off street parking spaces shall be provided for every residential unit,
commercial and office facility hereafter constructed or placed on a site within
the city as provided by section
9-5-4 of this code. The city council may reduce this requirement upon a showing
by the property owner that the requirement is excessive. A variance from the
parking requirement may be granted under circumstances where the applicant
provides funds to the city to acquire an equal number of city owned parking
spaces in the vicinity of the use. (Ord. 362, 3-7-2000; amd. 2004 Code)
6-4-8: VIOLATIONS; PENALTY:
The city may enforce these regulations through civil action and/or prosecution.
Violations of any provision of this chapter shall be misdemeanor punished as
provided in the general penalty in section
1-3-1 of this code. Each day of violation after notice shall constitute a
separate violation. (Ord. 362, 3-7-2000; amd. 2004 Code)
CHAPTER 5
PARKS, BEACHES AND WATERFRONT
SECTION:
6-5-1: City Parks
6-5-2: Beaches
6-5-3: Waterfront
6-5-1: CITY PARKS:
   A.   Camping In City Parks: Camping of any kind or nature in any city park
shall be and the same is hereby prohibited, said parks to be for daytime use
only. (1983 Code § 7.04.010; amd. 2004 Code)
   B.   Hours: The hours for use and occupancy of any city park shall be from
seven o'clock (7:00) A.M. until one o'clock (1:00) A.M. the following morning;
no persons except law enforcement officers or other officers or employees of
the city shall be present in any park area during the hours set out in this
subsection. (1983 Code § 7.04.020)
   C.   Standards Of Conduct:
      1.   All persons occupying a city park shall do so in an orderly and
sanitary manner, in full compliance with all laws of the state of Idaho and
ordinances, regulations and rules of the city relating to use and enjoyment of
said park areas;
      2.   All persons using any park shall do so in a manner so as not to
interfere with its use and enjoyment by other members of the public lawfully
using the same;
      3.   All parks shall be kept in a neat and orderly condition by all
persons using the same, and all garbage and refuse shall be cleaned up and
placed in proper receptacles by all patrons of the park premises;
      4.   All persons using any park shall refrain from loud or tumultuous
conduct, or the use of profanity; and
      5.   No person or persons shall be permitted to use any park while
intoxicated. (1983 Code § 7.04.030)
   D.   Violations; Penalty: Any person found guilty of violating the
provisions of this chapter shall be deemed guilty of a misdemeanor and, upon
conviction thereof, shall be punished as provided in the general penalty in
section
1-3-1 of this code. (1983 Code § 7.04.040)
6-5-2: BEACHES:
   A.   Definitions:
   BEACHES: Includes the public beaches of the city and all parking and grassy
areas adjacent thereto and belonging to the city.
   WATERFRONT: Includes all public swim areas, boating areas, docking areas and
docks situated thereto, extending from the beaches to the breakwater. (1983
Code § 7.08.010)
   B.   Recreational Use: The beaches and waterfront areas adjacent to and
belonging to the city shall be used for recreational purposes only. (1983 Code
§ 7.08.020)
   C.   Uses Prohibited:
      1.   Commercial Enterprises And Manufacturing: No manufacturing or
commercial enterprise or activities of any kind for profit shall be maintained
on, in or in connection with the beaches and waterfront area; nor shall such
property in any way be used for other than strictly recreational purposes. This
restriction shall not be construed, however, as preventing the city from
charging fees, rentals or other charges for the occupancy or use of any of the
beach or waterfront areas, or for any services provided by the city in
connection therewith. (1983 Code § 7.08.030)
      2.   Exhibitions, Festivals, Shows Or Fairs: No fair, exhibition,
festival, show or other activity that attracts or is intended to attract,
divert or collect a large number of persons shall be conducted or allowed on
the beaches or waterfront areas. (1983 Code § 7.08.040)
   D.   Exceptions; Permit Required: The restrictions of subsection C
notwithstanding, if application shall be made, in writing, to the city council
requesting relief from this section, and if the city council at any regular
meeting, or special meeting called for that purpose, shall determine that the
interests of the residents of the city and the general public will be served
thereby, then the city council reserves the right to grant to individuals or
organizations a permit to carry on an activity which would otherwise be in
violation of this section. The permit shall be subject to such terms and
conditions as the city council may deem fit and proper, with permit fees
established by resolution of the city council to be paid. (1983 Code §
7.08.050; amd. 2004 Code)
6-5-3: WATERFRONT:
   A.   Camping:
      1.   There shall be a fee charged for the use of camping facilities
belonging to the city and situated on the waterfront adjacent to the Harrison
marina, the amount thereof to be fixed by resolution of the city council. Such
amount may, as need arises, be adjusted from time to time by further resolution
of the city council. (1983 Code § 7.12.010)
      2.   The fees established by the city council shall be enforced on a
year-round basis, and payment of such fee shall be the joint and several
responsibility of any person causing a motor vehicle or recreational vehicle to
be parked in a camping space, and the person exercising control over such
vehicle. (1983 Code § 7.12.030)
      3.   The city council shall appoint its designated agent who shall have
the authority to collect the established fee from each person using the said
camping area. (1983 Code § 7.12.020)
   B.   Interference With Collection Agent: No person shall harass or assault
the appointed agent of the city council while he is acting in his capacity as
designated agent, nor shall any person interfere with the designated agent so
as to hinder him from carrying out his duties. (1983 Code § 7.12.050; amd. 2004
Code)
   C.   Violation; Penalty: If any person shall hinder the appointed collection
agent or refuse to pay the fee established hereunder, when payment of the same
is requested by the designated agent of the city council, and if it is
determined that the said fee was then due and owing from the individual so
refusing, then that individual shall be guilty of a misdemeanor, punished as
provided in the general penalty in section
1-3-1 of this code. (1983 Code § 7.12.040; amd. 2004 Code)
CHAPTER 6
CITY CEMETERY
SECTION:
6-6-1: Sale Of Cemetery Lots
6-6-2: Interment
6-6-3: Grave Openings
6-6-4: Monuments And Ornamentation
6-6-5: Compliance By Work Force
6-6-6: Prohibited Acts And Conditions
6-6-7: Violation; Penalty
6-6-1: SALE OF CEMETERY LOTS:
All lots and parcels of ground in the Harrison cemetery which the city shall
sell will be conveyed by certificate, giving the owner the right of possession
forever, as a place of interment of the dead; subject, however, to such rules
of the Harrison cemetery as shall be in force at the time of the purchase, or
that may be adopted thereafter for the general good of the cemetery. It is not
the intention to give credit for lots or graves, but in case such leniency is
shown, the city shall retain the right of ownership of the lots, and in case
the party purchasing the same should fail to pay the full amount due thereon,
the city may, after waiting a reasonable time, at its discretion, proceed to
remove the bodies therein to some other suitable place in the cemetery, or to
the portion set apart for single graves; or it may set apart that portion of
the lot in which the remains are buried and sell the remaining portion of the
lot. (1983 Code § 2.24.070)
6-6-2: INTERMENT:
   A.   Permit Required: Whenever an interment is to be made in a family lot,
written application must be made to the mayor or city clerk by the owner of
said lot, through the undertaker, and a permit obtained therefor. (1983 Code §
2.24.080)
   B.   Application And Contents:
      1.   The application must state the following particulars:
         a.   The full name of the deceased;
         b.   Age, if known;
         c.   Date and place of demise;
         d.   Date of interment and location of grave;
         e.   Name of undertaker;
         f.   Outside size of coffin or box.
      2.   In case of the interment of a deceased owner of a lot, the
application shall be authorized by some person known to the mayor or city clerk
to be of his family or household, or by his physician. (1983 Code § 2.24.090;
amd. 2004 Code)
   C.   Advance Notice Of Interment Required: The permit must be deposited with
the mayor at least four (4) hours before the time of the funeral, and notice of
the hour of the funeral must be given at the same time. (1983 Code § 2.24.100)
6-6-3: GRAVE OPENINGS:
   A.   Fees: All graves must be opened by the city, and all interments will be
subject to the charges as may be set from time to time by resolution of the
city council. (1983 Code § 2.24.130)
   B.   Removal Of Bodies: When a body is to be removed from one part of the
cemetery to another part of the cemetery or to another place of interment, a
permit must be obtained from the mayor prior to such removal. (1983 Code §
2.24.120)
   C.   Transfer From Other Burial Grounds: In all cases where bodies are
brought from other burial grounds for interment, the same proceedings must be
had before burial as provided in section
6-6-2 of this chapter. (1983 Code § 2.24.110)
6-6-4: MONUMENTS AND ORNAMENTATION:
   A.   Placement Of Monuments: No monument shall be placed on any lot without
permission of the mayor, and it shall be his duty to direct the location and
placement of the same, and no monument shall be so placed as to interfere with
any important effects upon adjoining lots. The foundation of all monuments and
headstones shall not be less than three feet (3') deep, and subject to approval
by the mayor. (1983 Code § 2.24.030)
   B.   Ornamentation:
      1.   Ornamental Objects: No lot shall contain any vase or seat, or any
rock works, or any other ornamental objects, excepting by permission of the
mayor. (1983 Code § 2.24.010)
      2.   Trees And Shrubs: No lot shall be decorated by its owner or other
parties interested therein with any tree or shrub without the permission of the
mayor. (1983 Code § 2.24.020)
      3.   Grounds: The mayor shall, under the direction of the city council,
have entire charge of the planting of trees and shrubs, in accordance with the
general plan for the ornamentation of the grounds; and if any tree or shrub
standing on any lot, whether planted by direction of the mayor or otherwise,
shall become, by means of its roots, branches or otherwise, detrimental to
adjacent lots or avenues, or for any reason its removal shall become necessary
or advisable, the mayor shall have the right, and it shall be his duty, to
remove such tree or shrub, or any part thereof. (1983 Code § 2.24.040)
      4.   Private Vaults And Tombs: Private vaults and tombs will be allowed
in lots where the ground is suitable therefor; but in every case a design of
the same must first be submitted to, and approved by, the city council. (1983
Code § 2.24.050)
6-6-5: COMPLIANCE BY WORK FORCE:
In every case where workers are employed by owners of lots to do work or make
improvements in or about said lots, such workers shall be subject to the
control and direction of the mayor; and any worker who shall neglect or refuse
to obey said direction, or who shall carelessly or wilfully do injury to
adjacent lots, or who shall neglect to remove any rubbish accumulated in his
work, will not thereafter be permitted to work in the grounds of the cemetery.
(1983 Code § 2.24.060)
6-6-6: PROHIBITED ACTS AND CONDITIONS:
   A.   Motor Vehicles: Fast driving and driving off the road or avenues in and
around the cemetery are strictly prohibited. (1983 Code § 2.24.140)
   B.   Animals: No animals will be permitted to enter the cemetery grounds.
(1983 Code § 2.24.150; amd. 2004 Code)
   C.   Disturbing The Peace: Boisterous and profane language, and any conduct
tending to disturb the quiet and good order of the place, are forbidden. (1983
Code § 2.24.160)
   D.   Picking Flowers; Defacing Property: Visitors and all other persons who
shall enter the grounds are forbidden to pick any flowers or plants, to break
or injure any tree or shrub, or to write upon or deface any wall, monument or
gravestone. (1983 Code § 2.24.170)
   E.   Loaded Vehicles: Loaded vehicles, unless loaded with material for work
in the cemetery, will not be permitted to enter the grounds. (1983 Code §
2.24.180)
   F.   Persons Removed From Cemetery: Any person violating any of the rules or
regulations established for the cemetery, or committing any offense, shall be
removed therefrom. (1983 Code § 2.24.190; amd. 2004 Code)
6-6-7: VIOLATION; PENALTY:
Any person who shall violate any of the provisions of this chapter shall be
deemed guilty of a misdemeanor and, upon conviction, shall be punished as
provided in the general penalty in section
1-3-1 of this code. (1983 Code § 2.24.200)
CHAPTER 7
FRANCHISES
SECTION:
6-7-1: Franchises Required
6-7-2: Conditions Of Franchise
6-7-3: Application For Franchise
6-7-4: Objections To Franchise
6-7-5: Granting Of Franchise
6-7-1: FRANCHISES REQUIRED:
Any person, company, corporation or association intending to construct or
erect, or causing to be constructed or erected within the corporate limits of
the city a telephone or telegraph line, electric, gas or other light plant, or
any system of waterworks, or any cable and/or telecommunications systems,
whereby any part or portion of any highway, bridge, street or alley in the city
limits will be used for the erection of poles, stretching of wires, laying
underground wires or laying of pipes for purposes of light plants, and laying
water pipes for a system of waterworks, must first obtain a permit or franchise
from the city council. (1983 Code § 5.20.010; amd. 2004 Code)
6-7-2: CONDITIONS OF FRANCHISE:
   A.   Term: No permit or franchise shall be granted for a longer period than
twenty (20) years
   B.   Exclusivity Prohibited: No franchise or permit shall be exclusive.
(1983 Code § 5.20.020)
6-7-3: APPLICATION FOR FRANCHISE:
   A.   Contents: The application for a franchise shall be presented to the
city council and shall state fully the person, company, corporation or
association applying for the permit or franchise, the object, purpose and
period for which the permit is requested. The privileges asked for must be
specifically stated; all highways, bridges, streets or alleys to be made use of
must be designated; and the mode of how the proposed line or system and the
extent of its plants, and how built, constructed or to be erected must be fully
described. The proposed rates and charges to patrons and consumers must be
stated; any concession in return for the permit to be made on the part of the
applicant to the city or its residents must be stated; and any other
information that will fully explain the terms, conditions and purposes under
which the permit is asked shall be embodied in such application. (1983 Code §
5.20.030; amd. 2004 Code)
   B.   Filing; City Council Action: After the filing of such application, the
city council shall cause an ordinance to be drawn up in conformity with the
application and also embodying therein such conditions, terms, regulations and
restrictions for the government, operation and construction of the respective
lines or systems as they may deem fit. Such ordinance shall be read three (3)
times before final action thereon is taken. (1983 Code § 5.20.040)
   C.   Notice:
      1.   After the filing of any application for a permit or franchise, the
applicant shall, at his own expense, cause to be published a notice that such
application has been made, and in such notice shall set forth the purpose, the
period for which such permit or franchise is asked, and the concessions,
conditions and terms under which such permit or franchise is asked. The
highways, bridges, streets and alleys to be used in the construction of the
lines or systems and the rates and charges proposed to be charged to patrons
and consumers shall be stated in the notice. (1983 Code § 5.20.050; amd. 2004
Code)
      2.   Such notice shall be published in the official newspaper of the city
for a period of not less than four (4) consecutive weeks. (1983 Code §
5.20.060)
6-7-4: OBJECTIONS TO FRANCHISE:
Upon the notice provided for in section
6-7-3 of this chapter being published, any resident of the city may file with
the city council any protest, remonstrance or objection against the granting of
such permit or franchise, such protest, remonstrance or objection to be in
writing and signed, and if the city council finds that a majority of the
property owners and taxable inhabitants in the city have signed such protest,
remonstrance or objection, such permit or franchise shall not be granted. (1983
Code § 5.20.070)
6-7-5: GRANTING OF FRANCHISE:
Should no majority of property owners and taxable inhabitants present protests,
remonstrances or objections, at the time when the ordinance for a permit or
franchise comes up for the third reading, such ordinance shall then come up for
final action, and in order to be passed, it shall require the affirmative vote
of one-half (1/2) plus one of the members of the full city council. (Ord. 316,
9-4-1990; amd. 2004 Code)
TITLE 7
PUBLIC UTILITIES
CHAPTER 1
WATER SYSTEM
SECTION:
7-1-1: Supervision
7-1-2: Installation And Maintenance Of Equipment
7-1-3: Separate Connections Required
7-1-4: Authority To Shut Off Water
7-1-5: Excavations For Connections
7-1-6: Tapping And Connection Permit
7-1-7: Water Meters Required
7-1-8: Water Service Reconnection Fee
7-1-9: Service Outside City
7-1-10: Supply To Fire Equipment
7-1-11: Shutoff Orders
7-1-12: Prohibited Acts And Conditions
7-1-13: Violation; Penalty
7-1-1: SUPERVISION:
   A.   City Maintenance Supervisor: The city maintenance supervisor shall be
the head of the water department and subject only to the orders of the mayor
and city council. The city maintenance supervisor, together with his assistant,
shall perform the duties prescribed herein for the water department of the
city, except such duties as may be specifically assigned to the city clerk as
the clerk of the water department 1 . (1983 Code § 14.20.010)
   B.   Water Department Personnel: The water department shall consist of the
city clerk as clerk of the water department, and the city maintenance
supervisor and his assistants, who shall carry out all the provisions of this
chapter and shall be subject only in matters of discretion to the mayor and
city council. (1983 Code § 14.20.020)
 
Notes
1 1. See section
  1-5-4 of this code.
7-1-2: INSTALLATION AND MAINTENANCE OF EQUIPMENT:
The water department will, at the expense of the city, run a service pipe not
larger than three-fourths inch (3/4") from the city water main to the lot line
of any applicant or consumer of water, provided that the distance is not
greater than seventy five feet (75'). All pipe of one inch (1") in size is to
be laid by and under the direction of the city water department, and the
expense thereof charged to the consumer or owner of the property served. The
water consumer, or the owner of the property served, shall at all times be
responsible for the condition of the lateral pipes, curb cock and box when
located on his premises, and said owner, or water consumer, shall be
responsible for all damages resulting from leaks or breaks to the service pipe
on his property. No claim shall be made against the city on account of the
breaking of any service pipe or apparatus, or for the failure in the supply of
water. The city will be responsible for repair of leaks that occur upon public
property. Where a break or leak occurs in a lateral service pipe, the property
owner or water consumer will be required to repair the pipe at his own expense
and to protect the city and the water department from any cost for such repair.
If, after being notified, the owner of the property upon which a break or leak
occurs or his agent does not make the necessary repairs to his lateral service
pipe immediately, the water department shall cause the water to be shut off
from said premises, and the same shall not be turned on until the service pipe
has been properly repaired and the owner or water consumer has paid to the city
the fees set out in chapter 5 of this title for the shutting off and turning on
of said water. Where a break or leak occurs in a lateral service pipe, the
property owner or water consumer shall be responsible for any and all damages
resulting therefrom. Where there is a leak and it is doubtful whether the water
is from a break in the city main or in a private service pipe or lateral line,
the city shall have charge of the repairs but the costs of repairs shall be
assessed to the proper private property owner or consumer in the event the leak
or break is in a service pipe or lateral line. (1983 Code § 14.20.030; amd.
Ord. 388, 6-3-2003)
7-1-3: SEPARATE CONNECTIONS REQUIRED:
   A.   The service pipes must be so arranged that the supply for each separate
house or premises may be controlled by a separate stopcock placed at a point
designated by the water department, and the owner or agent of said property
will be held responsible for all bills for water used through said service for
his use, or from the use of others to whom it may be accessible. Where water is
supplied on one service to several houses, families or persons, the city
council may require separate services or may permit the single service to be
used on condition that one designated person shall pay for all water used on
the service. (1983 Code § 14.10.080)
   B.   It is unlawful for any owner, agent or tenant to supply or permit to be
supplied any water to two (2) or more buildings through one and the same
connection, except on special contract with the water department. (1983 Code §
14.40.030)
7-1-4: AUTHORITY TO SHUT OFF WATER:
The water department reserves the right at any time to shut off, without
notice, the water from its mains for the purpose of making repairs or
extensions, or for any other purpose; and no claim shall be made against the
city by reason of the breakage of any service pipe or from any other damage
that may result from shutting off said water. (1983 Code § 14.20.040)
7-1-5: EXCAVATIONS FOR CONNECTIONS:
   A.   Safety Precautions Required: The streets must be opened in the manner
which will occasion the least inconvenience to the public. No excavation in any
street or alley shall be left open overnight unless properly guarded with amber
lights, which must be maintained from sunset to sunrise; and every precaution
must be taken to ensure public safety. (1983 Code § 14.20.050; amd. 2004 Code)
   B.   Excavation Permit: Before excavation within the streets, for the
purpose of laying service pipes or repairing the same, the owners of property
to be served, or their legal agent, must first, through the plumber doing the
work or by themselves, secure a permit for such work from the office of the
water department on a form provided for that purpose. Permit fees are as set by
resolution of the city council. (1983 Code § 14.20.060; amd. 2004 Code)
7-1-6: TAPPING AND CONNECTION PERMIT:
All applications for the tapping or connection with any water mains must be
made at the office of the clerk of the water department by owners of the
property to be served, or their legal agents, and be accompanied by an
application fee in an amount to be set by resolution of the city council. Said
applicant shall fully state all purposes for which the water is required, the
size and number of taps or other outlets from which the water is to be drawn,
and the number of the lot and block to which the water is to be taken and used
and the street from which it is desired that the service pipe shall be laid.
Such application shall show upon its face that the same is made and taken and
accepted subject to any and all rules and regulations then in force, or to be
made later, for the government and control of said waterworks system. No person
other than an authorized employee of the water department shall tap or make any
perforation or opening of any kind in any water main or any service pipe from
which water may be taken. (Ord. 419, 6-5-2007)
7-1-7: WATER METERS REQUIRED:
All property owners within the corporate limits of the city, in, on or upon
whose premises water is consumed by the owner, tenants or otherwise, must have
a water meter, to be furnished by the city, installed in, at and upon the
respective premises; and all city water used in, on or upon said premises shall
pass through and be measured by said water meter. In the event that any
property owner shall refuse to allow such water meter to be installed, it shall
be the duty of the water department to forthwith discontinue the water to the
premises or property of such owner, or to refuse to deliver water to the
property or premises of the owner. All property owners connected to the city
water system shall pay a user fee in the amount set by resolution of the city
council. (Ord. 410, 7-11-2006)
7-1-8: WATER SERVICE RECONNECTION FEE:
Whenever water service to a property being served by the system has been
terminated pursuant to section
7-1-11 of this chapter, a reconnection fee shall be paid to the city before
restoration of water service to the property. The amount of the reconnection
fee shall be established by resolution adopted by the city council, and shall
be subject to modification from time to time in the manner provided for the
modification of other rates established by this chapter. (Ord. 431, 3-3-2009)
7-1-9: SERVICE OUTSIDE CITY:
It shall be discretionary with the city council as to whether water service
shall be provided outside the city limits. (1983 Code § 14.30.030)
7-1-10: SUPPLY TO FIRE EQUIPMENT:
Water will be furnished to pipes or hoses, to be used for fire purposes only,
free of charge on the condition that the fire pipes, hoses or branches be
disconnected from all other water supplies furnished by the city and that all
pipes, hoses or branches so used be sealed to be broken open only in case of
fire. (1983 Code § 14.10.010)
7-1-11: SHUTOFF ORDERS:
All orders for discontinuing water service must be made in writing to the water
department and must be done in conjunction with termination of sewer service as
described in section
7-2-6 of this title. The owner may elect to continue paying at the unoccupied
rate set by resolution and subject to modification from time to time. If the
owner elects to cease paying the monthly fee, the city council will issue an
order terminating service. The order shall advise that the property is not
served by city utilities. Said order shall be filed with the county recorder to
provide notice to any individual considering the purchase of said property. The
capitalization fee, in effect at the time of reconnection, must be paid before
service will be reinstated. (Ord. 431, 3-3-2009)
7-1-12: PROHIBITED ACTS AND CONDITIONS:
   A.   Unauthorized Turn On: After the water has been turned off at the curb
cock, it shall not be turned on by any person except an employee of the water
department; and if so turned on at the curb cock by any person other than an
employee of the water department, the mayor shall have the water turned off at
the main and shall have charged against the property and the property owner a
penalty of five dollars ($5.00) which must be paid before the water shall again
be turned on, and in addition thereto, the party turning on said water in
violation of the provisions of this subsection may be punished for the
violation thereof as provided in the general penalty in section
1-3-1 of this code. (1983 Code § 14.40.010)
   B.   Contract Required: No person shall knowingly take or use or allow to be
used water without having previously contracted for the same. (1983 Code §
14.40.020)
   C.   Water Waste: It is unlawful for any owner, agent or tenant, or other
person to maintain, suffer or permit to remain in a leaky or defective
condition any water pipe, hydrant, service or water connection of any sort
whereby city water may be wasted; or cause the same to be maintained, suffered
or permitted to remain in a leaky or defective condition for more than twenty
four (24) hours after knowledge or discovery of the same; and it is unlawful
for any person to waste or cause to be wasted in any way whatsoever any water
from the water supply works of the city. If undue waste is permitted, or water
is bypassed to other consumers, or in cases of deception, misrepresentation or
abuse of the privilege of connection with the water system, the supply of water
shall be turned off without notice, and a penalty of five dollars ($5.00) shall
be paid to the water department before the water is turned on, and in addition
thereto the offending person may be punished as provided in the general penalty
in section
1-3-1 of this code. (1983 Code § 14.40.040)
   D.   Unauthorized Use: It is unlawful for any person to open, close, turn or
interfere with, or to attach to or connect with, any fire hydrant, curb cock or
valves, without permission from the water department, or to disturb or damage
any pipe, machinery, tools, or other property of the water department, or to
throw any substance into the reservoir or water main, or to bathe in any
reservoir, or to deface or injure any buildings belonging to or connected with
said water system. (1983 Code § 14.40.050)
   E.   Injure Or Defraud: It is unlawful to do any of the following acts with
intent to injure or defraud:
      1.   Obstruct, alter, injure or prevent the action of any meter or other
instrument used to measure or register the quantity of water supplied to a
consumer thereof;
      2.   Make any connection by means of a pipe, or otherwise, with any main
or pipe used for delivery of water to a consumer thereof in such a manner as to
take water from said main or pipe without its passage through the meter or
other instrument provided for registering the amount or quantity consumed, or
use any water so obtained;
      3.   Make any connection or reconnection with such main or pipe, or turn
off or on, or in any manner interfere with, any valve, stopcock or other
appliance connected therewith; or
      4.   Prevent by the erection of any device or construction, or by any
other means, free access to any meter or other instrument for registering or
measuring the amount of water consumed, or interfere with, obstruct or prevent
by any means, the reading or inspection of such meter or instrument by any of
the employees of the water department. (1983 Code § 14.40.060)
   F.   Restricted Use Of Washers And Sprinklers: No person shall use or permit
to be used any washer or lawn or garden sprinkler except upon his own premises
for which he has made application and is paying rent. (1983 Code § 14.40.070;
amd. 2004 Code)
   G.   Maximum Hose Size Permitted: No hose larger than three-fourths inch (3/
4") in diameter shall be used from any service pipe without special permission
from the water department, except in case of fire protection. (1983 Code §
14.40.080)
   H.   Use Of Water During Fire: No person shall draw any water from the city
main during a fire except for the extinguishment of a fire. (1983 Code §
14.40.090)
   I.   Water Pollution: No person shall cast, throw or place in any water
reservoir, supply pipe, water main, headworks or other part of the waterworks
or supply system of the city, any dirt, refuse, filth, wood, sticks, stones or
other substances or matter, or shall in any manner pollute the water in any
service supply pipe, headworks or any other part of said waterworks system.
(1983 Code § 14.40.100)
   J.   Connection Within Floodplain: Connection to the city water system is
prohibited for any properties located within the 100-year floodplain, or within
designated wetlands, unless a 404 permit has been issued by the U.S. army corps
of engineers. (Ord. 363, 2-1-2000; amd. 2004 Code)
7-1-13: VIOLATION; PENALTY:
Each and every person who shall violate any of the provisions of this chapter
shall be deemed guilty of a misdemeanor and, upon conviction thereof, shall be
punished as provided in the general penalty in section
1-3-1 of this code. (1983 Code § 14.40.110)
CHAPTER 1A
WATER SYSTEM
ARTICLE A. WATER RATES AND CHARGES
SECTION:
7-1A-1: Basic Rate Classes Established
7-1A-2: Computation Of Charges
7-1A-3: Rates
7-1A-4: Rate Regulations
7-1A-5: Financial Reports
7-1A-1: BASIC RATE CLASSES ESTABLISHED:
Separate basic rates and charges for furnishing water service shall be
established by the city council from time to time for each of the following
classes of users:
   A.   Occupied residential within the city.
   B.   Residential outside the city.
   C.   Commercial, multiple residential:
      1.   For any apartment building or similar commercial facility composed
of multiple dwelling units wherein persons reside on a permanent or semi-
permanent basis, the monthly base rate shall be assessed for each living unit
within said complex whether or not said units are actually occupied.
      2.   The above stated rate class shall not apply to motels, trailer
camps, or similar facilities providing accommodations to transients, which
facilities shall be classified as commercial property under subsection E of
this section.
   D.   Unoccupied residential structures.
   E.   Commercial (public retail, nonresidential).
   F.   Unoccupied commercial structures.
   G.   Industrial (any nongovernmental user of publicly owned treatment works
identified in the "Standard Industrial Classification Manual 1972", office of
management and budget, as amended and supplemented under the following
divisions:
 
Division A: Agriculture, forestry and fishing;
Division B: Mining;
Division D: Manufacturing;
Division E: Transportation, communications, electric, gas and sanitary
            services;
Division I: Services.
 
   A user in the divisions listed may be excluded if it is determined that it
will introduce primarily segregated domestic wastes or wastes from sanitary
conveniences. Rates to be established individually by contract to be
commensurate with other charges in the city; however, rates will comply with
the federal guidelines and/or regulations pursuant to the water pollution
control act.
   H.   The city reserves the right to determine the type of customer receiving
water service and to classify the type of customer within the foregoing
categories. The city further reserves the authority to delegate the duty to so
classify customers. In the event there arises a dispute relative to the type of
customer receiving water service and thus as to the applicable water service
rate, the city's determination as to the type of customer shall be binding upon
the customer in the absence of manifest error. A customer disputing the
classification shall have the right to appeal the determination of the city by
making a written request to the city council for a redetermination hearing and,
after a hearing on the matter, the determination of the city council shall be
likewise binding on the customer in the absence of manifest error.
   The written request for redetermination shall set forth with reasonable
clarity the reasons for the request. The redetermination hearing shall be held
at city hall at the next regularly scheduled meeting of the city council, or at
such time and place as the city council may order; provided, however, that any
hearing held other than at the next regularly scheduled meeting of the city
council or at the city hall shall be held only upon at least five (5) days'
written notice to the party requesting the hearing, setting forth the time and
place of hearing. At such hearing, either party may present witnesses and other
evidence, but a failure by the City to present witnesses or other evidence
shall in no way invalidate the decision of the City Council, it being the
requesting party's burden to convince the City Council that reclassification
should be made. All charges shall begin with the date of classification by the
City, rather than the date of any final appeal determination. (Ord. 323, 2-2-
1993)
   I.   Charges for the use of water from fire hydrants within the City shall
be one hundred fifty dollars ($150.00) for an annual hydrant use permit paid to
the City prior to use. Should it appear that said use will exceed ten thousand
(10,000) gallons, additional estimated water shall be billed to the permittee
at the City's normal monthly rate. (Ord. 390, 6-3-2003)
7-1A-2: COMPUTATION OF CHARGES:
   A.   All fees and charges are subject to modification by resolution upon
review by the City Council of the revenues and costs of the water system, which
review shall be carried out at least once during any given twelve (12) month
period of operation of the system.
   B.   Charges based on water consumption shall be computed on the monthly
average over the previous twelve (12) month period, with an adjustment at the
end of each twelve (12) month period. The adjusted average shall be the basis
for the succeeding twelve (12) month period. In the event that any unit of
occupancy does not have a twelve (12) month record of water consumption,
billing shall be estimated and agreed upon between the City and the customer,
until such a record is available, and adjustment for the previous twelve (12)
month period shall be made at that time. (Ord. 323, 2-2-1993)
7-1A-3: RATES:
   A.   General: Water rates within the City charged by the Water Department
shall, subject to the minimums established by the City Council, be as follows:
 
First 7,500 gallons used for residential users     $0.35/1,000 gallons
Over first 7,500 gallons used for commercial users 0.60/1,000 gallons
 
   (1983 Code § 14.10.120)
   B.   Unmetered Premises: Rates for unmetered premises will be determined by
an agreement between the City Council and the owner or occupant of such
premises, structure or establishment as to the estimated amount of use. (1983
Code § 14.10.130)
7-1A-4: RATE REGULATIONS:
   A.   Minimum Basic Rates Within City: The basic minimum rate for water
furnished by the City to each classification of water user within the City,
created by section
7-1A-1 of this article, and the quantity of water to which the minimum basic
rate applies, shall be set from time to time by resolution adopted by the City
Council.
   B.   Excess Usage: In addition to the minimum basic rates provided for in
this article, the City Council shall, from time to time, by resolution adopted
by it, establish rates for excess water usage for each class of property
created by section
7-1A-1 of this article. (Ord. 323, 2-2-1993)
   C.   Time Of Charge: Water rentals at the established rate will be charged
against the property from the date on which the water is turned on until the
date on which the water meter is removed. (1983 Code § 14.10.050)
   D.   Water Use For Building Purposes: Contractors, builders or others
desiring water for building purposes must make application to the Clerk of the
Water Department prior to using same, and the amount to be paid shall be based
upon the rates fixed therefor by the City Council. (1983 Code § 14.10.070)
   E.   Rates Outside City: The basic minimum rate for water furnished by the
City to water consumers outside the City shall be set from time to time by
resolution of the City Council. (1983 Code § 14.10.100)
7-1A-5: FINANCIAL REPORTS:
The City Clerk shall be the Clerk of the Water Department and shall, before the
first meeting of the City Council in each month, render to the Mayor a
statement covering the previous month which shall contain the names of all
water users and consumers, the amount of water rent charged to each consumer
together with the amount paid or unpaid by each consumer. The statement shall,
after its inspection by the Mayor, be filed as a public record in the Office of
the City Clerk. (Ord. 2019-477, 6-4-2019)
CHAPTER 2
SEWER SYSTEM
SECTION:

7-2-1: DEFINITIONS:
Unless the context specifically indicates otherwise, the naming of terms used
in this chapter shall be as set forth in this section. Terms not specifically
defined herein shall be as defined in the publication "Glossary Water And
Wastewater Control Engineer", 1969, published by the American Public Health
Association, American Society of Civil Engineers, American Water Works
Association, and Water Pollution Control Federation.
ASTM: Represents the American Society for Testing Materials.
AGENCY: Any city, town, county or state.
BOD OR BIOCHEMICAL OXYGEN DEMAND: The quantity of oxygen utilized in the
biochemical oxidation of organic matter under standard laboratory procedure in
five (5) days at twenty degrees centigrade (20°C), expressed in milligrams per
liter.
CAPPING PERMIT: A permit required for the disconnection of sewer service.
CITY: The city of Harrison, a municipal corporation of Kootenai County, state
of Idaho.
CITY COUNCIL: The Harrison city council, the governing body of the city.
CITY SEWERAGE SYSTEM: The system of conduits, pumps, treatment plants and
structures used for the purpose of conveying from their source, treating in any
manner, and conveying to final points of disposal all wastes of any nature
permitted by this chapter to enter said system.
CLUSTER LIVING UNITS: Living units, such as trailers, cabins or houses which
have utilities operated and maintained by an association or by a common owner.
COMMERCIAL SERVICE: All sanitary sewerage system service other than domestic
service.
COUNTY: Kootenai County, Idaho.
COVER: The depth of material lying between the top of the sewer or drain and
the finished grade immediately above it.
DOMESTIC SERVICE: Any sanitary sewer system serving a living unit.
DOWNSPOUT: A pipe which conducts water from a roof of a building or structure.
GARBAGE: Putrescible waste from the preparation, cooking and dispensing of food
and from the handling, storage and sale of produce.
INSIDE CONNECTION: The side of the sewer constructed on private property from
the plumbing outlet to the individual pump unit.
MULTIPLE DWELLING: A multiple-family dwelling; namely, a building designed and/
or used to house two (2) or more families living independently of each other
and including all necessary household functions of each such family, such as
motels and apartments.
NATURAL OUTLET: Any outlet into a watercourse, pond, ditch, lake, bay or other
body of surface or ground water.
OTHER STRUCTURE: Any building other than a single-family or multiple dwelling.
OUTSIDE CONNECTION: Any sewer constructed in a public right of way and where
the public agency who has jurisdiction or such right of way requires a permit
fee or any other charge.
PERSON: Any individual, company, partnership, corporation, association, society
or group, and the singular term shall include the plural.
pH: The logarithm of the reciprocal of the weight of hydrogen ions in grams per
liter of solution.
PLUMBING OUTLET: In plumbing, the part of the lowest horizontal piping of a
drainage system that received the discharge from soil, waste and other drainage
pipes inside the walls of the building and conveys it to the side sewer (house
connection). The latter begins thirty inches (30") outside the inner face of
the building wall.
PROPERLY SHREDDED GARBAGE: Garbage which has been shredded to such degree that
all particles will be carried freely under the flow conditions normally
prevailing in public sewers, with no particle greater than one-half inch (1/2")
in any dimension.
PUBLIC SEWER: Any sanitary sewers, including, but not limited to, trunks,
laterals, stubs and force mains and being constructed by the city or any person
within the public right of way or perpetual easement obtained by the city.
SANITARY SEWAGE: Wastewater derived from domestic, commercial and industrial
wastes and to which storm, surface and ground waters are not intentionally
admitted.
SANITARY SEWER: A sewer which carries sanitary sewage.
SEWAGE: A comprehensive term including industrial waste, storm drainage and
wastewater.
SHALL/MAY: "Shall" is mandatory; "may" is permissive.
SIDE SEWER: A sanitary sewer pipe leading from a plumbing outlet, drain, or
other facility to the stub sewer of the public sewer system.
SINGLE-FAMILY DWELLING: A structure designed and/or used to house a single
family.
STANDARD SPECIFICATIONS: Those specifications contained in a bound volume
entitled "Standard Specifications And Standard Details", published by URS/Hill,
Ingman, Chase, Consulting Engineers of Seattle, Washington, consisting of
printed material and standard details, latest edition with revisions.
STORM DRAIN: A public or private drain which carries storm and surface waters
or drainage effluent from storm plumbing outlets and other unpolluted water.
STRUCTURE: Anything constructed or erected, the use of which requires location
or attachment to something having location on the ground, and shall in
addition, include, but not be limited to, trailers, mobile homes and house
trailers, but shall not include fences and walls.
STUB SEWER: A sewer constructed from the lateral or truck sewer to the property
line or edge of perpetual easement of the property being served.
SUSPENDED SOLIDS: Solids that either float on the surface of, or are in
suspension in water, wastewater or other liquids, and which are largely
removable by laboratory filtering.
UNPOLLUTED WATER: Water in its natural state, or water which after use for any
purpose, is not substantially changed as to chemical or biochemical qualities.
WASTEWATER: The spent water of a community. From the standing of source, it may
be a combination of the liquid and water carried wastes from residence and
commercial buildings, industrial plants and institutions, together with any
ground water, surface water and stormwater that may be present. (1983 Code §
13.01.010)
7-2-2: USE OF PUBLIC SEWERS:
   A.   Use Required:
      1.   Time To Connect:
         a.   The owner or owners of all houses, buildings or properties used
for human occupancy, employment, recreation or other purpose, situated within
the city, shall be and they are hereby required to install all suitable toilet
facilities therein, and to connect such facilities directly with the proper
public sewer, provided said public sanitary sewer is located where it is
possible or practicable for such owner or owners to make such connection,
practicality thereof to be determined by the city council. Unless otherwise
determined upon the written application of the owner or owners, any facilities
located within three hundred feet (300') of the sewage line shall be deemed to
be located where it is possible and practicable to make the said connection.
         b.   If a public sewer is not available for connection, the owner or
owners of all houses, buildings or properties used for human occupancy,
employment, recreation or other purpose, situated within the city, shall be and
they are hereby required to install a septic tank and drainfield system for the
purpose of sewage treatment and disposal. The design and construction of said
facilities shall be in conformance with the rules and regulations of the
Panhandle health district or its equivalent, including all requirements as to
fees, permits and inspections. (1983 Code § 13.04.010)
      2.   Connection Within Floodplain: Connection to the city sewer system
for property located within the 100-year floodplain or any connection to
property within a designated wetland is hereby prohibited unless a 404 permit
has been issued by the U.S. Army Corps of Engineers. (Ord. 363, 2-1-2000)
   B.   Connection And Charges: The owner shall connect all applicable plumbing
outlets to the public sewer at his expense at the point designated by the city.
In the event it shall be necessary for the city to serve notice upon the owner
to make said connection, the owner shall, within a period of thirty (30) days
after the date of mailing or personal service of notice to the property owner
directing such connection, make application to the city for a permit in the
manner hereinafter specified.
   Such owner or owners, at the time of application for a side sewer permit and
prior to making said sewer connection with a public sewer as herein prescribed,
shall pay the appropriate and proper fee therefor, which fee shall be set from
time to time by resolution of the city council. Final connection to the public
sewer system shall be made within the period specified in the connection
permit. (1983 Code § 13.04.020)
   C.   Connection Within City Limits: All plumbing outlets from any building
or structure hereafter constructed or made available for human occupation and/
or use for any purpose shall, when required by this section, be connected to a
public sewer of the city before the completion of the construction of such
building or structure or before any occupancy or use thereof is allowed. In the
event that a public sewer capable of serving that building or structure has not
been completed by the city prior to the construction or occupancy of such
building or structure, said building or structure shall be connected to the
public sewer within ninety (90) days after written notification of public sewer
availability. In any event, written application for a permit to connect, as
hereinafter required, shall be made at least thirty (30) days prior to the
anticipated date of connection, or at least thirty (30) days prior to such
other date as may be provided for by these rules and regulations, whichever is
earlier. (1983 Code § 13.04.030)
   D.   Connection Outside City Limits: All connections to the city's public
sewer, whether within the city's boundaries or without, shall be subject to the
rules and requirements herein and such as may be established with regard
thereto, with the exception that connections made outside the city limits shall
be made on a voluntary basis. (1983 Code § 13.04.040)
   E.   Notification Of Connection And Charges: The city shall mail to the
owner a notice that sewer service is available and all applicable service
charges shall begin the first day of the month that begins thirty (30) days
after the mailing of such notice. (1983 Code § 13.04.060)
7-2-3: REPAIRS BY OWNER:
   A.   Notice To Repair:
      1.   Any needed repair to that portion of the side sewer lying between
the pump facility and the structure or connection to a public sewer shall be
made within thirty (30) days after the date of mailing or personal service of a
notice to the owner of the property served notifying such owner to make such
repair. In the event of an emergency, the city may establish a shorter period
of time for the repair to be made or, if the owner cannot be located or does
not promptly make such repairs, the city may make the repairs as provided for
in subsection B of this section. (1983 Code § 13.04.050)
      2.   A repair permit shall be obtained from the city office for the
repair of any minor portion of an existing side sewer on an appropriate form
provided by the city. If the repair is not minor, the city may require the
replacement of the existing side sewer. A repair is not minor if the integrity
of the side sewer is impaired. (1983 Code § 13.12.060)
   B.   Failure To Repair: After the giving of notice as required herein, the
city attorney may be authorized by the city council to bring suit against the
owner or other responsible person, to compel said owner or responsible person
to make the connection provided in this chapter, to authorize the city to make
the connection, or for such other relief as may be appropriate. The suit may
obligate the owner to pay the city's costs, disbursements and reasonable
attorney fees. After the giving of notice as required herein, the city attorney
may be authorized by the city council to bring suit against the owner, or other
responsible person, to make the needed repair to that portion of the side sewer
lying between the pump facility and the structure, if roots or any other cause
has created a blockage, as provided in subsection A of this section, to
authorize the city to make the repair at the expense of the owner or other
responsible person or for such other relief as may be appropriate. The suit may
obligate the owner or other responsible person to pay the city's costs,
disbursements and reasonable attorney fees. (1983 Code § 13.08.010)
7-2-4: SIDE SEWER PERMITS AND FEES:
   A.   Permit Application And Issuance:
      1.   Prior to the construction of any new house, building or structure or
the connection of any existing house, building or structure to the public sewer
or the making of any repairs, alterations or additions to any side sewer or
line connected thereto, an application for a side sewer on an appropriate form
provided by the city shall be filed by the owner or his agent at the city
office. The permit application shall be supplemented by any plans,
specifications or other information considered pertinent in the judgment of the
city. Upon approval of the application, the city shall issue a side sewer
permit to the applicant, which permit shall be authorization to proceed to
connect and/or construct in accordance with the permit. If the applicant
proceeds in any manner other than as authorized, the city may require the
applicant to redo any work that is not in accordance with the permit.
      2.   Any permit to connect any existing house, building or structure
shall be valid for ninety (90) days, unless extended or renewed by the city
upon good cause being shown upon application therefor, prior to the original
expiration date. A renewal permit shall be valid for not more than thirty (30)
days.
      3.   Any permit to connect any new house, building or structure to the
public sewer shall be valid for the duration of the associated building permit,
unless extended or renewed by the city upon good cause being shown upon
application therefor, prior to the original expiration date. A renewal permit
shall be valid for not more than ninety (90) days.
      4.   All permit applications shall be submitted to the city at least
thirty (30) days prior to the commencement of any construction, and shall be
accompanied by an application fee in an amount set by resolution of the city
council.
   B.   Exhibition Of Permit: Any permit required in accordance with this code
shall at all times during the performance of the work, and until completion
thereof and approval by the city, be posted in some conspicuous place at or
near the work and must be readily and safely accessible to the city's
representative. (Ord. 419, 6-5-2007)
7-2-5: INSTALLATION REGULATIONS:
   A.   Installation: A property owner may install the side sewer on his own
property provided he complies with the applicable provisions of this chapter. A
side sewer contractor, registered in accordance with section
7-2-8 of this chapter, shall be required for any work on public rights of way
and/or any connection to the main line sewer. Should the owner or occupant
choose to employ a bonded side sewer contractor to do the work on his property,
such contractor shall obtain the permit in his own name. (1983 Code §
13.12.030)
   B.   Community Side Sewer: Whenever a side sewer is to be located on
property other than the property being served, the owner or owners of the side
sewer shall secure a written easement on an appropriate form provided by the
city covering and granting the right to occupy such property and such purpose
and for the city to enter such easement for purpose of maintaining the side
sewer. The written easement shall be recorded by the owner of the residence in
the office of the county auditor and a copy of same be furnished to the city
prior to issuance of a permit. (1983 Code § 13.12.040)
   C.   Side Sewer: The owner(s) of property being served by a side sewer shall
grant an easement to the city to enter upon the property being served for
maintaining the side sewer and the individual effluent pump unit. This
subsection shall be subject to any and all applicable laws, whether of the
state of Idaho or the United States. (1983 Code § 13.12.050)
   D.   Nonconforming Installations: Nonconforming installations shall not be
permitted without the express approval of the city, and all releases required
by the city shall be obtained in writing by the person requesting such
installation. (1983 Code § 13.12.090)
7-2-6: CAPPING:
When any property owner desires to have sewer service terminated as to any
property belonging to said owner because the building or structure thereon is
either removed, destroyed or condemned, whether by public health authorities or
by a public entity having the power of condemnation, the side sewer shall be
capped. All orders for discontinuation of sewer service must be done in writing
by the owner and must be in conjunction with termination of water service as
described in section
7-1-11 of this title. Owner may elect to continue paying at the unoccupied rate
set from time to time by resolution and subject to modification from time to
time. If owner elects to cease paying the monthly fee city council will issue
an order terminating services. The order shall advise that the property is not
presently served by city utilities. Said order shall be filed with the county
recorder to provide notice to any individual considering the purchase of said
property. The capitalization fee, in effect at the time of reconnection, must
be paid before service will be reinstated. (Ord. 431, 3-3-2009)
7-2-7: INSPECTIONS:
No person shall cover or backfill any side sewer, public sewer, grease or sand
trap or screen without having called for an inspection, and permission and
approval therefor having been received from the city; nor shall any garbage
grinder larger than three-fourths (3/4) horsepower be placed in operation prior
to having called for an inspection and permission and approval therefor having
been received from the city. The city shall be given twenty four (24) hours'
notice when such construction is ready for inspection. If any person covers or
backfills any of the above without having obtained approval, the city may
require the person to uncover the work so that a proper inspection and approval
can be made. The city shall have access at reasonable times to all single-
family, multiple dwellings and other structures for the purpose of examining
any and all plumbing outlets and/or side sewers for the purpose of ascertaining
whether the provisions of this chapter are being complied with.
   A.   Materials And Workmanship: The city shall inspect and make such tests
deemed necessary to ensure that the new construction meets all requirements of
this chapter in respect to materials and workmanship.
   B.   Testing: The city shall require all sewer construction to be tested by
a water exfilteration test in accordance with these regulations. (1983 Code §
13.12.080)
7-2-8: CONTRACTORS TO BE REGISTERED:
Any side sewer contractor performing any work within and with the approval of
the city, must be licensed with the state of Idaho pursuant to the public works
contractors license act 1 , and must provide the city with proof of his
registration. In addition, any contractor wishing to be approved by the city
shall submit an application on a form provided by the city requesting such
approval. (1983 Code § 13.16.010)
 
Notes
1 1. IC § 54-1901 et seq.
7-2-9: WORK IN PUBLIC RIGHTS OF WAY:
   A.   Construction: No person shall install stub sewers in any public or
private thoroughfare or right of way unless he is registered with the city
pursuant to section
7-2-8 of this chapter, and has complied with all of the requirements of this
chapter. Any work on rights of way shall be in conformity with the requirements
of the agency having jurisdiction over such rights of way. It will be the
contractor's responsibility to notify the appropriate authorities before
beginning work on the right of way and to ascertain that the schedule of
operation proposed is satisfactory to the agency; provided, however, that all
work must be completed with dispatch and in a reasonable time. If a person has
received notice from the appropriate agency or the city that certain work must
be done and that person fails to do said work, the city may complete the work
and charge the cost thereof to the person responsible. (1983 Code § 13.20.010)
   B.   Protection: Any excavation made by any sewer contractor with the proper
authority, in a right of way immediately adjacent thereto, shall be protected
and guarded by fencing or covering with proper lights. The protection of the
public from the danger of such excavation shall be the responsibility of the
sewer contractor; and the contractor shall be liable for any damage caused by
his failure to properly protect and guard such excavation as herein required.
If the contractor fails to properly protect and guard such excavation as herein
required, the city may properly protect and guard such excavation and charge
the cost thereof to the sewer contractor who shall, upon receiving written
notice of the amount of such charge, immediately pay the same to the city.
(1983 Code § 13.20.020)
   C.   Maintenance:
      1.   Whenever construction work under this chapter is undertaken on
easements or rights of way over private property or public rights of way or
franchise, all work shall be confined to the limits of such easements, rights
of way or franchise and accomplished to cause the least amount of disturbance
and a minimum amount of damage.
      2.   The contractor shall make his own arrangements with the person or
property owner for whom he is working as to how the work is to be conducted and
scheduled. The contractor shall also reach an understanding with the property
owner as to what condition the owner's property is to be left in upon
completion of construction. The aforesaid arrangements shall be completed prior
to the commencement of work.
      3.   The contractor shall not remove, even temporarily, any trees or
shrubs which exist on private or public property or in parking strips without
first having notified the property owner or authorities maintaining same. If
necessary to remove trees, shrubs, etc., the contractor shall restore the same
to an equal or better condition satisfactory to the property owner and the
city. (1983 Code § 13.20.030)
7-2-10: CONSTRUCTION STANDARDS:
   A.   Plumbing Contractors: No plumbing contractor shall make connections of
side sewers to public sewers of the city without first being registered with
the state of Idaho pursuant to Idaho Code 54-2601 et seq.
   B.   Standards For Low Pressure Lines: The following standards are only for
low pressure lines and not intended for high pressure mains. High pressure
mains shall meet ASTM specifications or equivalent:
      1.   Compliance Required: Connection shall be made as directed by the
city and will be made at the point designated by the city. All plumbing outlets
shall be connected to the sanitary sewer.
      2.   Grade And Depth: All side sewers shall be laid on not less than two
percent (2%) (2'/100') grade nor more than two hundred percent (200%) (2'
vertical; 1' horizontal) grade. Side sewers shall not be laid less than thirty
inches (30") from any foundation wall of any building and, if there is no
foundation wall, not less than thirty inches (30") from the outer lines of any
footings, pilings or building supports. Minimum cover shall be not less than
forty eight inches (48") at the curb line, the property line or private
property. Any side sewer laid generally parallel to the curb line shall have
not less than forty eight inches (48") of cover, and all cover measurements
shall be based on the established grade or on existing improvements.
      3.   Alignment: The side sewer shall be laid at uniform grade and in
straight alignment so far as is possible. Changes in direction shall be made
only with curved pipe with no greater than forty five degree (45°) bends. The
connection to the building drain and combination bends of ninety degrees (90°)
shall include a cleanout. All pipe shall be laid on a firm earth bedding
containing no material larger than one inch (1"). If the trench bottom contains
mud or water, the pipe shall be laid on a four inch (4") granular base of
three-fourths inch (3/4") minus rock, pea gravel, sand or combination thereof.
Backfill around the pipe and to a point four inches (4") above shall be
selected trenchside material hand placed and hand tamped, with no material
larger than one inch (1").
      4.   Design Standards: Unless otherwise called for, side sewer pipe shall
be plastic and meet the following specifications:
 
*Plastic ASTM        D-2241, D-1785
         (Class 125)
 
   *Bedding, laying and joining to be done in accordance with the
manufacturer's recommendations.
      5.   Sewer Pipe Size: A one and one-half inch (11/2") side sewer shall be
required for all service connections.
      6.   Cleanouts: A cleanout is required whenever more than a one-eighth
(1/8) (45°) bend is used. Also, immediately outside the house or structure
where the city deems necessary.
      7.   Water Line Location: No water line shall be laid in any form or
manner in the same ditch line as the sewer line. The side sewer must be
installed so as not to interfere or be constructed within three feet (3') of
any water line used for human consumption.
   C.   Septic Tanks:
      1.   Septic tanks used in the city for new construction or replacements
after the effective date hereof shall meet the following minimum sizes:
 
1 - 4 bedroom home      1,000 gallons
Each additional bedroom 250 gallons of capacity shall be added to the tank
 
      2.   Septic tanks shall be constructed by a recognized tank precaster, of
concrete or other corrosion resistant material to then current design
standards, unless otherwise approved by the city.
   D.   Trailer And Mobile Living Unit Connections: Sewer connections for
trailers and other mobile living units shall be of a type approved by the city,
but in all cases shall be above grade and shall have the ability to be made
airtight and watertight when not in use. (Ord. 371, 6-5-2001)
7-2-11: GRAFTS TO PUBLIC SEWERS:
   A.   Wye Or Tee Not Found: If a wye or tee is not found at the measurement
given by the city, the contractor shall prospect five feet (5') in all
directions from the measurement given, and if not found, then notify the city.
(1983 Code § 13.28.010)
   B.   Saddles: Unless otherwise specified by the city, prefabricated saddles
will be used for any graft to the public sewer. No graft will take place unless
the city representative is present. (1983 Code § 13.28.020)
7-2-12: DISCHARGES TO SEWERS:
   A.   Storm Or Other Waters: No person shall discharge, permit or cause to be
discharged any storm drainage water, surface water, groundwater, roof runoff,
subsurface drainage or cooling water to or in any sanitary sewer. (1983 Code §
13.32.010)
   B.   Other Substances: Except as hereinafter provided, no person shall
